 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />Oh, that's nonsense!</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />It's true. It explains why there are so many bachelors. In the second place, I won't give you my permission.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />Your permission?</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />My dear fellow, Gwendolen is my first cousin, and before I allow you to marry her, you will have to explain about… Cecily.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />Cecily? What do you mean? Who is Cecily? I don't know any one called Cecily.</p> 
 <p>(A bell rings)</p> 
 <p><strong>Lane</strong><br />You called, sir?</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />Bring me that cigarette case Mr Worthing left here last Thursday.</p> 
 <p><strong>Lane</strong><br />Yes, sir.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />Have you had my cigarette case all this time? I wish you'd told me. I've been to the police. I nearly offered a large reward.</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />Well, I wish you would. I'm quite&nbsp;<strong>hard up</strong>&nbsp;at the moment.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />There's no point offering a large reward now it's been found.</p> 
 <p><strong>Lane</strong><br />The cigarette case, sir.</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />I think that's rather mean of you, Ernest. However, it's not important now because according to the&nbsp;<strong>inscription</strong>&nbsp;inside, the case isn't yours anyway.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />Of course it's mine. You've seen me use it hundreds of times. Now, could I have my cigarette case back?</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />Yes, but this isn't your cigarette case. It's a present from someone called Cecily, and you said you didn't know anyone of that name.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />Well, actually, Cecily is my aunt.</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />Your aunt!</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />Yes. Lovely old lady she is, too. Lives in Tunbridge Wells.</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />But why does she call herself &quot;little Cecily&quot; if she is your aunt? &quot;From little Cecily with her&nbsp;<strong>fondest</strong>&nbsp;love.&quot;</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />What's wrong with that? Some aunts are tall, some are small.</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />Yes. But why does your aunt call you her uncle? &quot;From little Cecily, with her fondest love to her dear Uncle Jack.&quot; There is no problem, I admit, to an aunt being small, but why should an aunt call her own nephew… uncle? Besides, your name isn't Jack. It's Ernest.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />It isn't Ernest. It's Jack.</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />You have always told me it was Ernest. I have introduced you to everyone as Ernest. You look as if your name was Ernest. You are the most&nbsp;<strong>earnest</strong>-looking person I ever saw in my life – so honest and serious.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Ah yes, we should just say that the name Ernest was very common at the time, and the adjective 'earnest' – which sounds exactly the same - means, well, honest and serious.</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />Here, it's written on your card: &quot;Mr Ernest Worthing, B4, The Albany.&quot;</p> 
 <p><strong>Jack</strong><br />Well, my name is Ernest in town and Jack in the country, and the cigarette case was given to me in the country.</p> 
 <p><strong>Algernon</strong><br />Yes, but that doesn't explain why your small Aunt Cecily calls you her dear uncle. Or why you have two names to start with. Come on, you'll have to explain.</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>The Vicar of Altarnum has just told me he knows who murdered my uncle and aunt. I look at him in&nbsp;<strong>horror</strong>, and slowly, the awful truth becomes clear...</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Yes, Mary. I planned the&nbsp;<strong>wrecks</strong>. Your uncle followed my&nbsp;<strong>orders&nbsp;</strong>but they thought&nbsp;<em>he</em>&nbsp;was the leader. He loved that. No one knew about me. But then you came and asked questions.&nbsp;<strong>They had to die because of that</strong>... The end was near in any case. The fool got drunk on Christmas Eve. Well, you saw what happened... the whole country knew what he'd done. With a rope round his neck, he'd have told them about me.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>At least my uncle didn't lie - he talked and dreamt about his crimes. You... you hid yours behind the cross and the face of a priest. But why are you telling me all this now?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>I know you found the picture... I saw it had been moved. It frightened you, didn't it? &quot;Who is this strange man?&quot; you thought. Yes, Mary I am strange. Oh, but they listened to me in church and followed me like sheep.</p> 
 <p>Now, get ready. We've got to leave.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>We?!</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Yes, you're coming with me - you'll be a good&nbsp;<strong>companion</strong>. I've admired your courage since we first met.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>And if I don't come with you?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>You're no fool, Mary. There are no houses nearby and your screams won't be heard.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>You know that I'll run away at the first village.</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>You won't be able to.&nbsp;<strong>There aren't any villages on the Cornish coast because of the steep cliffs</strong>... just birds, and when we're on the ship...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>You're leaving England?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Of course - we'll go to Spain, to Africa... Get ready now.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I think quickly. I look at the clock... Jem will have reached the&nbsp;<strong>blacksmith</strong>&nbsp;and will know the truth.&nbsp;<strong>He'll realise I'm in serious danger so he will follow us</strong>... If I go with the vicar, at least I'll slow him down a bit, so Jem will have a chance to catch up...</p> 
 <p>I have no choice in any case.<strong>&nbsp;</strong></p> 
 <p>We cross the dark, empty moor quickly, avoiding the roads. The moon is hidden behind clouds... The Vicar has luck on his side.</p> 
 <p>As the ground becomes softer, we slow down... The&nbsp;<strong>marshes</strong>&nbsp;lie waiting. The Vicar knows, as I do, that&nbsp;<strong>one wrong step will result in a horrible death</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oh, where is Jem?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Whoah! &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>A wall of fog rises in front of us.</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>It's no good. We can't see anything. We'll have to wait until light. We'll sleep here... on these rocks, out of the wind.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I&nbsp;<strong>drift in and out</strong>&nbsp;of sleep.</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Shhh! Be quiet!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I'm woken by his cold hand on my mouth.</p> 
 <p>I can still hear the wind, but there is something else, too...</p> 
 <p>We leave the horses and he&nbsp;<strong>drags&nbsp;</strong>me higher and higher...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I can't go any further.</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Stay here, then.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>The last I see of him - he's standing on a rock with his arms stretched out...</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>(gunshot) Aaaah!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I look up. Jem is about 100 metres away behind a rock with a gun.</p> 
 <p>I haven't seen Jem since he shot the vicar. The Bassat family have been looking after me. They've asked me to stay and look after their children... but I&nbsp;<strong>long for</strong>&nbsp;the green fields and valleys of Helford. I'm walking for the last time on the moor. Tomorrow I'll go back and live quietly on the farm.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Someone is coming this way... but I can't see who because the sun is in my eyes...</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Hello Mary. I heard you're going to go and live at North Hill?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>They've asked me, but no... I'm going back to Helford tomorrow... And you, are you leaving Cornwall?</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Yes, I'm going to start a new life... I've got my whole home with me here. I may go north. Perhaps I'll&nbsp;<strong>breed</strong>&nbsp;horses instead of stealing them. Come with me, Mary.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I miss my home in Helford... I want to see the trees and animals...</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Go then and live on your farm.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>That's not very kind.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>I speak unkindly to my horses when they're&nbsp;<strong>obstinate</strong>. it doesn't mean I don't love them. Well, I'll be on my way... Goodbye Mary.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Wait! Are you saying you love me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Maybe... It'll be a hard life.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I know, I'll take my chance... and we'll be together.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>So, I cross the moor for the last time - and for the first time, it looks beautiful in the sunshine. Behind me lies Jamaica Inn, empty, no more secrets - they have all been told... my new life is about to begin.</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I'm at the Vicar's house. I'm here because last night, when I returned to the inn, I found my uncle – dead... lying on the floor with a knife in his back. When Mr Bassat arrived with his men, they found my aunt's body upstairs... she'd also been&nbsp;<strong>stabbed</strong>.</p> 
 <p>The vicar suggested I stay with him. He came to the inn as soon as he read my note. He's not here. He left before I woke up.</p> 
 <p>While I've been waiting for him, I've been thinking about who the killer could be. Mr Bassat asked me if I had an idea who it was. I told him I didn't... but that's not true... I remember how Jem told me that he hated his brother... so they'll catch and hang him... or else he'll ride away, laughing at me. Either way, I know that I love him.</p> 
 <p>Strange how this room is so empty... No books, no paintings... Not like the vicar's house in Helford where I lived with my mother... His living room had pictures of smiling angels and village scenes... and piles of books on the desk.</p> 
 <p>There's nothing on this desk. I know... I'll write and ask if I can stay with him. Now, where's a pen and paper? Ah... in this drawer perhaps. That's&nbsp;<strong>odd!&nbsp;</strong>Nothing in the drawer, wait, there&nbsp;<em>is</em>&nbsp;a piece of paper... oh but it's already got something on it... a picture – by the vicar &shy;&shy;– his initials are there. What a strange picture.</p> 
 <p>It makes me&nbsp;<strong>shiver</strong>... It's the village church with the vicar and his&nbsp;<strong>congregation</strong>... but all the people have got sheep's heads and look stupid. The vicar has drawn himself as a wolf but not an ordinary wolf, a laughing wolf... What does it mean...? Oh no! He's back... quick! I shut the drawer quickly and sit by the fire. I'm shaking.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oh, Vicar...</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Did I&nbsp;<strong>startle</strong>&nbsp;you? I'm sorry I was so long. My horse was&nbsp;<strong>lame</strong>. You must be hungry?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I find it difficult to speak... The picture has shocked me. The vicar asks me to get the food from the kitchen. When I return, there are papers all over the desk. He's been burning letters.</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Don't you want to know what I've been doing today?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I'm sorry - I haven't thanked you for your kindness last night.&nbsp;<strong>If you hadn't taken me in, I wouldn't have had anywhere to stay.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Well... I've been to North Hill. Mr Bassat invited me and others to discuss the murder.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Does Mr Bassat&nbsp;<strong>suspect</strong>&nbsp;anyone?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>They've found the man, Harry... He can't be the murderer though.&nbsp;<strong>He would have been a suspect if he hadn't been locked up in the room by the bar for the last few days.</strong>&nbsp;But he said that someone else gave your uncle orders. This person must be the murderer. Don't you agree?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Well... er... Yes, I suppose...</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>It can't be one of the men. This person is clever. He must have come to the inn and he knows the moor well. He probably lives nearby. Did anyone like this come to the inn?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Er... no... I can't think...&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Why do you look so anxious, Mary? But I forgot... I saw a friend of yours today at North Hill.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I have no friends except you...</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>But you told me you went to Launceston with your uncle's brother...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I froze... I didn't know what to say...</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>He gave me a message for you. Tell her that &quot;I'm sorry&quot;. I...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Jem was at North Hill? Why?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Well, he's the dead man's brother. He wasn't upset, though...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Was Mr Bassat asking him questions?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>They've been talking all day. He's got brains - more than his brother. You told me he lives nearby, and steals horses?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I can't look at him, but I feel his eyes studying my face... He knows the truth.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>What will they do to him, Mr Davey?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>'Do'? What do you mean? I'm sure he won't be punished since he has helped them.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>'Helped'? I don't understand.</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Mary, it was Jem who&nbsp;<strong>informed</strong>&nbsp;Mr Bassat about his own brother. They left Launceston together after the horse market. Mr Bassat told him he could go free if he gave them&nbsp;<strong>proof&nbsp;</strong>about his brother and he did.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I can't believe it... I was so sure...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oh, Vicar, I'm such a fool... Where is Jem now?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>He's gone to find the&nbsp;<strong>blacksmith</strong>... He found a&nbsp;<strong>nail</strong>&nbsp;in the field by the inn. It must belong to the killer's horse. Only one person went to the blacksmith yesterday...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>How do you know?</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Because I know who that person was.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>His strange eyes are staring at me... I can't breathe! He knows who the murderer is!</p> 
 <p>Meet me in the next episode when I finally discover the shocking truth about who killed my aunt and uncle at Jamaica Inn. I am also in danger but who will come to my rescue?</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>It's morning…I have just woken up in my bed in Jamaica Inn. Memories of what I saw on Christmas Eve&nbsp;<strong>haunt&nbsp;</strong>me like a&nbsp;<strong>nightmare</strong>&nbsp;…</p> 
 <p>My uncle forced me to travel with him and his drunken men on Christmas Eve. I was so tired on the journey that while they were singing drunken songs, I fell asleep.</p> 
 <p><strong>When I woke up, they had gone</strong>. The carriage doors were locked, but I escaped through the window.</p> 
 <p><strong>They had brought me to the coast.</strong>&nbsp;It was a cold,&nbsp;<strong>misty</strong>&nbsp;night, but from where I was standing on the clifftop, I could see my uncle and his&nbsp;<strong>gang</strong>&nbsp;below on the shore, silent and still. They were watching the&nbsp;<strong>tide</strong>&nbsp;coming in, like a beast waiting to&nbsp;<strong>pounce</strong>.</p> 
 <p>The mist began to clear and a light appeared on a nearby cliff. At last!&nbsp;<strong>The officers the vicar had spoken about were coming!</strong>&nbsp;… But my hope disappeared quickly. &nbsp;… Another light appeared out at sea. This one was moving up and down… I realised then with horror what was happening. The light on the cliff was a&nbsp;<strong>trap</strong>!</p> 
 <p>A huge black shape appeared out of the darkness. Like a&nbsp;<strong>moth</strong>&nbsp;to a candle, the ship was heading for the rocks…</p> 
 <p>I remember now how I ran to the shore, how I screamed and shouted… but my uncle caught me and tied my hands so I couldn't move. I couldn't do anything except watch the disaster happen.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>The men splashed about in the water grabbing<strong>&nbsp;treasures that had fallen</strong>&nbsp;from the ship<strong>.&nbsp;</strong>Bodies were floating on the water. The men fell on them and took everything of value … even rings on the fingers. Hours passed. Light was appearing in the sky. My uncle saw it too.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Whoah!! … Stop everyone! Look!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>He pointed to the sky.</p> 
 <p><strong>Harry<br /></strong>Just … going …&nbsp;to get …</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Leave it! … There's no time!… It's getting light … Get out of here!… … before it's too late.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>But no one was listening. They were greedily grabbing what they could.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong><strong>My uncle had fired his pistol</strong>&nbsp;in the air. The men looked up and saw the sky. Fear struck them and they ran up the beach, carrying what they could… They knew they had stayed too long. Morning was their enemy. … I was too weak to move, but my uncle picked me up and carried me… In the&nbsp;<strong>panic</strong>, the carriage overturned. That meant there was only one small cart for everyone's escape.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Stand back!… I say stand back!…Harry, make sure no one moves… Shoot if necessary… I said…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>There was blood everywhere…two men lay still… I&nbsp;<strong>fainted</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary, are you awake?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>How long have I been lying here?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Two days.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Why didn't you wake me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary…I…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I've got to get up …</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Where are you going? Your uncle is downstairs.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>He doesn't frighten me… I must go and find….</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>He's never been like this before. He's locked all the doors. He's afraid of someone … I don't know who…</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Don't go down, Mary, he's got a gun…!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>All the doors and windows are&nbsp;<strong>bolted</strong>. My uncle is sitting in the kitchen…</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>I heard noises outside. Did you hear anything?...</p> 
 <p>He'll come… He warned me but I didn't listen…We didn't plan it this time.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>What do you mean? Who warned you? The officers?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Them…? They can't touch me. They need&nbsp;<strong>proof</strong>&nbsp;and all they have is a broken ship and two bodies. I wasn't there, was I&nbsp; – I was at home with my wife and niece cosy by the fire… No, it's him… He'll murder us all…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I don't understand. My uncle planned the wrecks, didn't he… or did he? Was there someone else who gave the orders? Who is he so afraid of?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Why don't we get away quickly now?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>You idiot! There are people everywhere who know what I've done. They'd like to see me hang … we'll stay till night time, when it's dark… We'll leave then!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I go along with my uncle's plan, but in my mind I'm making other plans – I'll escape somehow and find the vicar…. He's my only hope....</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I've hardly slept since my uncle's shocking&nbsp;<strong>confession</strong>&nbsp;- how he&nbsp;<strong>lures&nbsp;</strong>ships onto the rocks and drowns women and children.  <p><strong>Jem&nbsp;<br /></strong>It's Christmas Eve, Mary. Why so quiet? What's happened?</p>

 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oh, Vicar, it's you…&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>Come, I'll take you home.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>Once again I tell him my story … the market, Jem's disappearance… His glass eyes show no expression…&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>You are young… don't cry over him…&nbsp;</p> 
 <p>Am I right that it's quiet at Jamaica Inn…?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>My uncle has been drinking. He talks… Vicar, do you know what&nbsp;<strong>wreckers</strong>&nbsp;are?&nbsp;</p>

 <p><strong>Mary&nbsp;<br /></strong>What's happening…?&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>A gun is pointing at me. I see a face I recognise – the eyes look crazy and mad…&nbsp;<strong>it can only be one person</strong>…&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss&nbsp;<br /></strong>Get out! Ahh, so you've come back! What do you think you're doing at this time of night… on the road! Been with a man, I suppose.&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary&nbsp;<br /></strong>Don't touch me! You're a murderer and a thief and I've been to Launceston today to&nbsp;<strong>inform</strong>&nbsp;on you.&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Get back, you fools! She's lying… Get the horse Harry. The wind has changed… We'll use it…</p>

 <p>You're coming with us!&nbsp;<strong>We might not get far</strong>&nbsp;but we won't stay here waiting to be caught! Away!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>Where we are going, I don't know. But I can see from the look in my uncle's eyes that something very bad is going to happen.&nbsp;</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>There was nothing but a few&nbsp;<strong>sacks</strong>&nbsp;and the rope in the locked room. My uncle has returned and is very angry about Mr Bassat's visit.  <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>I think not.&nbsp;<strong>If there was a body, the police would surely investigate</strong>&nbsp;– but that's unlikely now. Could it be your imagination? All you saw was a piece of rope.</p>

 <p><strong>Vicar<br /></strong>People threaten others every day. Listen: you can talk to me any time.</p>

 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I don't know what you mean.</p>

 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Something like that, but I'm not afraid of you.&nbsp;<strong>I'd even like you if you didn't remind me of your brother</strong>.</p>

 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I must get back.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Are you coming with me to Launceston on Christmas Eve? I want to sell this pony.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong><strong>And if you're caught selling a stolen pony, I'll go to prison like you.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>I won't be caught. Come, don't you like a bit of excitement?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Well... where shall we meet?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>It's late when I get back and my uncle is lying drunk in the kitchen, surrounded by empty bottles. My aunt is in bed.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Who's there? Put away that knife!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Uncle Joss, it's me, Mary.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Mary - where are they?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>There's no one here. What's wrong, Uncle Joss?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>They can't hurt me now. They're all dead. Sit by me, Mary…&nbsp;It's this drink! I've killed men with my own hands. But&nbsp;<strong>when I'm drunk I'm afraid.</strong>&nbsp;I see them in my dreams, floating on the water... The ship: it was on the rocks but the water was flat and they were coming into the shore alive! We had to kill them all. One woman – she was holding on to some wood with her child. The water was only up to her shoulder. She cried out to me to help her: I took a stone and smashed her with it. I watched her and her child&nbsp;<strong>drown</strong>&nbsp;in four feet of water. We killed them all with stones and rocks.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>My blood turns cold, and I feel sick. My uncle is a murderer&nbsp;- that I suspected, but what he has just told me&nbsp;<strong>chills me to the bone.&nbsp;</strong>What terrible crime will he carry out next?</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I now know that my uncle is involved in smuggling. I also&nbsp;<strong>suspect</strong>&nbsp;that he has murdered a man. But if I tell, my aunt will suffer, so I can't do anything. Today, I am alone cleaning the kitchen. But the quiet does not last...</p>

 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>This is my chance to tell an officer about Joss - but look at my aunt. She is trembling and terrified.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Just say Joss is away.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary, you won't tell Mr Bassat about the wagons, will you? If anything happens to Joss, I'll kill myself.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>You took your time. Where's the landlord?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>He's not here. &nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>When will he be back?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>He went out after breakfast. I don't know when he's&nbsp;<strong>getting back.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong><strong>Damn!&nbsp;</strong>Listen to me – your husband is giving this whole area - my land - a bad&nbsp;<strong>reputation</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>I don't know what you mean. We live a quiet life here&nbsp;- my niece will tell you!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>I'm not a fool. We'll look around now we are here.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>Mr Bassat is having a good look around the inn. He knows there is something hidden here.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>This place is a&nbsp;<strong>disgrace</strong>! Call yourself an inn! There isn't one clean room.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary, Mary -&nbsp;the room by the bar!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>We come to the locked room.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I'm afraid this room is locked.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>Why?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I don't know…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>Have you ever heard wheels and horses at night?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>No, never.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>Where is the key to the room?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>My uncle has it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>Well, we'll have to&nbsp;<strong>break down</strong>&nbsp;the door, then.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I'm afraid. I hate lying to save my uncle -&nbsp;and part of me will be glad if they find&nbsp;<strong>evidence&nbsp;</strong>of his crimes. "<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I've not seen my uncle much since I arrived. I am glad because he's got a violent temper and treats my aunt badly. This morning, I've been exploring the country around the inn…</p> 
 <p>There is nothing but&nbsp;<strong>heather&nbsp;</strong>and grass for miles. In the distance I can see the&nbsp;<strong>marsh.&nbsp;</strong>It was in this wild and lonely land that my uncle lived as a boy with his two brothers. Last night he told me their story.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>If you had lived here, you would have taken to drink, like I did… it makes you do things. I had a family once: a father, mother, two brothers, but&nbsp;<strong>each one of them</strong>&nbsp;disappeared one way or another. My father was&nbsp;<strong>hanged</strong>. He killed a man. My brother Jem is clever – but they'll catch him, too and hang him. My brother Matthew – well, he drowned in the marsh. They found him one summer when the marsh dried up…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator</strong><br />When I get back to the inn my uncle is there...</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Well, did you miss me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Did you have a nice trip?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Nice,&nbsp;<strong>be</strong>&nbsp;<strong>damned</strong>. I've been riding for four days. There was a bit of money involved - that's all I care about.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Well, I'll go and help my aunt...</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>It's me you'll be helping tonight, in the bar...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>It's Saturday night – the bar is crowded. The air is full of smoke and the smell of unwashed bodies.&nbsp;<strong>All of them</strong>&nbsp;are drunk. Some men are so drunk that they lie on the benches like dead men.</p> 
 <p><strong>Harry (man in bar)<br /></strong>Another pint…</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Hurry up there, girl.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Uncle, I cannot&nbsp;<strong>bear</strong>&nbsp;this. I'm going upstairs.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Too good for us are you? Well it's almost midnight now. Go to your room and lock your door …</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oww! Let go of my wrist! You're hurting me!</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Hear this: Keep your mouth shut, and you won't get hurt - but if you start to ask...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oh! What's that noise? It's coming from under my room…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>The moonlight pours into my room creating ghostly shadows. I creep over to the window. My uncle is below and I recognise other men from earlier this evening. There are four or five&nbsp;<strong>wagons.</strong>&nbsp;The men have been taking big boxes from them into the inn.</p> 
 <p><strong>Harry<br /></strong>That's the last of them.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Good. Get going now. Be quick…</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>What will you do about him?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Don't worry. Harry and I will deal with him later…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I understand now. They are&nbsp;<strong>smuggling!</strong>&nbsp;Jamaica Inn is a perfect place for it. But what's my uncle doing at the moment? I have to go and see…</p> 
 <p>As I get closer to the bar, I hear voices. I hide in the shadows.</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>No, and no again – I will not be a part of it - that's murder you are talking about Mr Merlyn … killing&nbsp;<strong>innocent</strong>&nbsp;women and children – no!</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Not so fast! By God, you will do as I say. Another man said the same and he was hanging at the end of a rope a few minutes later! Harry – you go and lock the door behind you. I'll finish here…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I feel sick. My heart has been beating so loudly, I am sure they have heard it. I go back to my room quietly…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>What shall I do? If I had a gun or a knife, I could perhaps hurt my uncle so that the man can escape…But I have nothing …I must do something, though ….</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I creep downstairs again. The door to the bar is shut. There is silence. I suddenly know I have to open the door to find out.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>There's no one here! Just the tables and a few empty glasses…The door is open at the back. But wait… what's that hanging in the middle of the room? It's swinging… A rope hanging from a hook in the ceiling! But there's nothing on the end of it. What's happened to that man? I fear the worst…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator</strong><br />Next time we meet, an interesting visitor arrives at Jamaica Inn. But who is he and can he be trusted?</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I have arrived at Jamaica Inn to live with my aunt. My uncle is landlord here. It's a cold and lonely place. I'm at the door and I'm waiting for someone to let me in…</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Who's there?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>It's me. Mary. Mary Yellan.</p> 
 <p>[Heavy door opening]</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Ah, so, you've arrived at last. Well, say hello to your Uncle Joss.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Where is my Aunt Patience?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>What's the hurry? Don't you want to give me a big kiss first? Patience! She's here. [impatiently] Where are you, woman?</p> 
 <p>Patience! Where in hell is that woman?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>I'm here. Is it the girl?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>See for yourself.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>A woman with grey hair hurries towards me. In the candlelight her face is pale. She looks afraid.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Aunt Patience - I am so glad to see you.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>But she is unrecognisable. Her curls have gone and her happy smile also. I can see that&nbsp;<strong>she's been crying</strong>. This woman is old and anxious. She starts to cry.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Stop&nbsp;<strong>whimpering</strong>, woman. Can't you see the girl is hungry! I'll take her things up to her room. If there's nothing to eat on the table when I come down, you'll soon have something to cry about.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>He lifts my heavy box as if it's a bag of feathers. He is huge with shoulders like those of a bear.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>The kitchen is full of smoke from the fire. There are&nbsp;<strong>stains</strong>&nbsp;on the stone floor and there's a strong smell of alcohol. On the table there are two empty bottles of&nbsp;<strong>brandy</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>You mustn't mind your Uncle Joss. Some people find him strange at first, but he is very&nbsp;<strong>respected</strong>&nbsp;here. Just yesterday he told me that a man stopped and told him how much he admired.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Are you talking rubbish again woman? Sit down Mary. Eat. Listen, Mary. I'm in charge here and you'll do as I say. You'll serve the customers in the bar and help in the house. But if you open your mouth and&nbsp;<strong>squawk</strong>&nbsp;like a hen, you'll be sorry.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I'll help you like you say, but if you hurt my aunt, I'll tell and you'll be&nbsp;<strong>punished</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Patience, go and get me another bottle and be quick. Big words – maybe we're not so different, Mary. Here, drink this.This is my&nbsp;<strong>curse</strong>, Mary – drink.&nbsp;<strong>I've been drinking a little today but</strong>&nbsp;- Oh you'll see how we drink here some Saturdays – they hear the shouting and singing far away. People are afraid of me but I'm afraid of no one. Go to bed now.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>He suddenly grabs my wrist.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Listen carefully. Some nights you'll hear wheels, footsteps and voices outside. You must stay in your room and put your blanket over your ears. If you ask questions, I'll break every bone in your body. Do you understand?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>My room is small and&nbsp;<strong>bare.&nbsp;</strong>Just a bed and a table with a broken mirror. I feel lonely and&nbsp;<strong>trapped&nbsp;</strong>like a bird in a cage. But it's not too late to run away. I&nbsp;<strong>creep</strong>&nbsp;down the dark passage.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>[to herself] Who's crying? It must be my aunt!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I turn back. My uncle frightens me but I must stay and protect Aunt Patience.</p> 
 <p>I did not sleep well last night. My bed is hard and the blanket is thin. The house is quiet this morning. I'll look for a place to wash downstairs. Here is the bar. Ah, there's a passage here – maybe it's along here. A&nbsp;door – this must be the washroom.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>How strange – it's locked.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary! What are you doing?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Why is this room locked, Aunt Patience? What's in it?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>My aunt looks quickly behind her and her eyes are like a frightened rabbit's.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Is it because of the people who come to the inn at night?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary. Mary.<strong>&nbsp;I've been worrying about how to tell you this</strong>. I must warn you. Bad things happen here. Men come at night and they go into that room with Joss. When you hear them, you must stay in your room. You must never ask me or your uncle about it again.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>What is in this room and why is my Aunt so scared? I'm not going to like it here but I must stay to support her and keep her safe. Next time we meet – I have to work in the bar of Jamaica Inn on Saturday night where I get to meet a group of rough and drunk men. Later that night there are some strange goings-on in the yard outside.&nbsp; What's going on at Jamaica Inn?</p> 
 "
"<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>My name is Mary, Mary Yellan. I'm 23 years old.&nbsp;<strong>I'm not usually very brave, but I feel brave today.</strong>&nbsp;Here I am… on this long journey to Cornwall… on my own.&nbsp;<strong>I've left the farm</strong>&nbsp;where&nbsp;<strong>I've lived all my life</strong>. I wanted to stay there, but last week I made a promise to my dear Mother…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>[coughing/weak voice] Mary, my child… listen… I won't be in this world much longer.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Don't say that, Mother.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>It's true, Mary. But, before I go,&nbsp;<strong>I have only one wish</strong>…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Yes, Mother dear?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>When I die, promise me you will go and live with my sister, Patience.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>But why can't I stay here on the farm, here in Helford?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>You can't stay here alone.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>But&nbsp;<strong>I haven't seen Patience since I was a child</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>I know, but soon she will be the only family you have. [coughing]&nbsp;<strong>I have written to her. She has agreed</strong>&nbsp;that you can go and live with her and your uncle Joshua.&nbsp;<strong>They live on Bodmin Moor in Cornwall</strong>. Here, take her letter.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Bodmin Moor! But that's so far away!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>Mother died last Tuesday. The funeral was yesterday. We buried her next to Papa.&nbsp;<strong>Now, I'm on my way to my aunt's house.&nbsp; I've got the letter here</strong>…</p> 
 <p>[reading]<strong>&nbsp;Joss and I now live in Jamaica Inn</strong>, where he is&nbsp;<strong>landlord</strong>. It's on the road between Bodmin and Launceston…</p> 
 <p>This journey is so long! We have been travelling for hours. What a wild and lonely county Cornwall is. My only&nbsp;<strong>consolation&nbsp;</strong>is that I will see my aunt again after so many years. Oh how pretty she was with her golden hair and blue eyes! Always laughing, enjoying ourselves…</p> 
 <p>But&nbsp;<strong>I never visited her&nbsp;</strong>and I never met her husband either. … Ah, at last, I can see houses and people – this must be Bodmin town.</p> 
 <p>There is just me and one other traveller left. It's so cold and grey outside…&nbsp;<strong>The rain is lashing against the window</strong>. I wish it would stop! All I can see is mile upon mile of empty&nbsp;<strong>moorland</strong>. No trees… no houses… I wonder how many more hours we have to travel?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Excuse me, sir – is it much further?</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong><strong>Where are you going?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Jamaica Inn…&nbsp;<strong>Do you know it?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>Maybe I do and maybe I don't… and&nbsp;<strong>why are you going there?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I'm going to live there… with my aunt and uncle.</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>That will be Joss Merlyn...&nbsp;<strong>People say that queer things go on at Jamaica Inn</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong><strong>What do you mean – queer?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>It's just what they say. But&nbsp;<strong>respectable people don't go there any more</strong>. It's a lonely place.</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>If I were you, Miss,&nbsp; I would go on to Launceston tonight and go back to Bodmin tomorrow.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>But I can't.<strong>&nbsp;My aunt and uncle are waiting for me.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>Jamaica Inn is no place for a young woman.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I have nowhere else to go…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>What can he mean by 'queer things'?&nbsp;<strong>Why is he looking at me in that curious way?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Driver<br /></strong>Whoa boy…! Slow now.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong><strong>Why have we stopped here</strong>&nbsp;– it's the middle of nowhere?</p> 
 <p><strong>Driver<br /></strong>Jamaica Inn! There you go Miss.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>But there's nothing here! Oh – what's that? There up on the&nbsp;<strong>moor</strong>&nbsp;- a dark building with tall chimneys. I can see a path to the door. There's a sign twisting in the wind. It says 'Jamaica Inn'.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>Suddenly&nbsp;<strong>I feel frightened. I want to climb back in the coach.</strong></p> 
 <p>Too late –&nbsp;<strong>it's already gone</strong>... I suppose my only choice now is to enter Jamaica Inn.</p> 
 <p>Next time we meet – I get to meet my Aunt Patience and Uncle Joss. I discover what a mean and scary man my uncle is. And I discover a locked room – what is inside? &nbsp;&nbsp;</p>

"<p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Day 73 – we were sailing through a huge hurricane when a massive wave hit us. Oh why did I <strong>try to sail</strong> through this storm? I was <strong>hoping to get</strong> back home in 80 days but that seems impossible now. I must make sure my crew is ok – I need them now more than ever…</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Is everyone OK?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Oh, ouch, my arm. Passepartout, are you OK down there?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Where I am? Who am I?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>You're Passepartout – you're on a yacht and we were hit by a big wave.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Oh yes… I knew that… of course… a big wave. Let me just get up… oh my legs… right, I need to inspect the damage.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Well, Peggy the parrot seems OK.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Hooray! Well the satnav is still working but there's a tear in the front sail and everything in the galley is underwater.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>I'm so sorry. I <strong>wanted to carry on</strong> through the storm – but I was wrong.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>It's OK Phil. I thought you were very courageous, very brave. Look we're still alive. We've just got to get back to London, and with the money you'll get, we… I mean you… can <strong>enjoy living</strong> the rest of your life.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Oh Sophia, thank you, I'm so glad we found you.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>We won’t be going anywhere with this damage.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>We must try Passepartout – never give up!</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>I don't know where all my courage and determination has come from but I like it! We are now sailing across the Atlantic – it doesn't seem as big and scary anymore. We've sailed past the Azores – we couldn't <strong>stop to have</strong> a rest – and now we're not far from the coastline of Britain, but we've run into some thick fog and we can’t see where we're going. I can hear the foghorn of a lighthouse but we are all so tired, weary and exhausted from our trip that we're… falling… asleep.</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>What's that? We've hit something. We're sinking.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Oh no, look, water, water. Abandon ship, abandon ship! Get the lifebelts.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Quick, set off one of those emergency flares – we need help.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Oh no, The Mermaid is sinking, farewell.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>We've <strong>failed to get back</strong> home in 80 days. Disaster! We didn’t reach the pub in London on time and we've lost Tom's yacht – the yacht I was <strong>supposed to win</strong> and then sell to make some money. But we're alive and we have been rescued by a lifeboat. It's taking us to shore where we can make our way to the station, catch a train to London and hopefully meet our friends in the Horse and Groom pub.</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>John<br /></span></strong>Phil – goodness, we'd forgotten all about you. And you, Pete.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>We have been sailing around the world for 80 days… We’ve nearly faced death and you have forgotten about us?!</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom<br /></span></strong>He's just joking. It's great to see you again: let me get you a drink and you can tell me all about your adventure but, hold on, who's your new companion?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>This is Sophia – we met her in Sao Tome and she's helped us sail around the world.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom<br /></span></strong>Pleased to meet you Sophia.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Sorry we're a day late.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom<br /></span></strong>A day late? You mean it's day 81? Oh well. In that case, the yacht is still mine. A bet is a bet!</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Ahh… well, about that. Your yacht… The Mermaid… she's wonderful…. I mean, she was wonderful… we had an accident… we hit some rocks and sank.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom<br /></span></strong>You're joking?!</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Errr… he's not.We sank off the coast of Cornwall this morning.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Tom wasn't pleased to hear the news about his yacht. I <strong>was hoping to win</strong> our bet. But here we are, with no yacht and no money - and I have to write a story about how we <strong>failed to sail</strong> around the world in 80 days.</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Excuse me. Can everyone <strong>stop talking</strong> for a moment – I have an important announcement. I've just double-checked our route on the computer and I realised that at zero degrees west and zero degrees east we crossed the International Date Line.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom<br /></span></strong>Very interesting, Pete – but so what?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Well when you cross that line you gain an extra day – that means today is only day 80, not day 81!</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>You're right Passepartout – today is day 80. We're on time! What would I do without you?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>So does that mean Phil has won the challenge after all?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom<br /></span></strong>Well… erm… I suppose so. You went around the world in 80 days – but did you <strong>stop to collect</strong> the things on your challenge list?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>I… we got them all. Look… Morna music from Cape Verde, cacao beans from Sao Tome, Bourbon Pointu coffee from Reunion Island, a conch shell from… well we don't know where really, a Savi mask from Papua New Guinea, and a pahu drum from Tahiti.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom<br /></span></strong>Impressive! Congratulations – but I'm afraid you still don’t get a prize – that was my yacht, and you sank it.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>It's OK. I don't really need it. I've decided there's something much more important. Sophia… I'm so glad we rescued you… I've grown very fond of you and I <strong>don’t want to lose</strong> you… I know it's going to be complicated but… will you marry me?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Oh gosh… well, yes! You're my hero – give me a kiss.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Oh dear… I suppose I <strong>get to keep</strong> the parrot?</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Dear Diary – My adventure is going to make a great story. I'm <strong>hoping to sell</strong> lots of books this time. Sometimes you need a big adventure to change your life. Even when your journey doesn't go to plan you just learn so much. Luckily for me, I've won a great prize – a loyal friend in Passepartout, and Sophia, a new friend and wife. It's good to be home.</em></p>

"<p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>It's day 61 – and it's a miracle! I didn't hit any rocks and we're safe in the harbour at Papeete on the island of Tahiti. It’s just a quick stop to clean up the yacht and take on fresh water. <strong>I'm going to find</strong> one more souvenir to take home as part of my challenge – some type of musical instrument – hmmm. And how are my travelling companions? Well, they're not under the weather anymore – I mean, they aren't feeling ill – they've recovered from the food poisoning that I unfortunately gave them – but strangely, they still seem very pleased with me.</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>'Aloha' Phil! There you are, we were looking for you.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Hi. I thought you two should rest, so I went off to buy something. Look, I've bought a 'pahu' – it's a traditional Tahitian drum. I need some kind of exotic instrument as part of my challenge – so here we go. And my credit card works here, so I’ve bought us all some colourful Polynesian shirts – don't they look great?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Brilliant – Ilove the palm trees…</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>I suppose I could wear it at sea where nobody could see me.</p>

 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>I really don't know. I sold everything to pay for my trip. I'm going to have to find somewhere to live as soon as I get back to the UK.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Don't worry Sophia. Phil has a sofa you can sleep on! There's room for that parrot too. And <strong>I'm going to start</strong> looking for a new job as soon as we get home – Captain of the QE2 maybe?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Ah look, we're finally out of the canal. This must be the Caribbean Sea. It's beautiful and it's calm too – there aren't any waves. Look, it looks like a swimming pool.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>That's because there's no wind. We'll have to use the engine for a while until the wind gets up.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Day 71 – it's windy. Very, very windy. A radio message has warned us of a hurricane heading our way. The sea is already getting rough. It's time to batten down the hatches and prepare for another very bumpy ride. I'm getting quite used to this!</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>This is wild! We've got to change course – find some shelter.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Yes, you're right. Our sails will just rip to pieces in this weather.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>No – I think we should carry on. We've been in worse seas than this. And we can't waste any more time. Come on everyone, we can't let this little storm beat us. <strong>We're going to get through this</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Are you feeling ok Phil?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>I'm feeling great.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>For once I feel like I know what I'm doing. I'm not scared. I’ve got Passepartout, Sophia and our lucky parrot Peggy with me –and that makes me think <strong>everything is going to be ok</strong>. I hope I'm right!</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>OK Phil, maybe it's the captain's hat - but you really are a changed man. Come on then, let's ride this storm.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Hold on tight – there's a huge wave coming.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>All<br /></span></strong>Whoooahhhh!</p>

"<p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>It's day 50. We've made it to Papua New Guinea and <strong>the capital city</strong> of Port Moresby. <strong>People</strong> here seem to be wearing <strong>masks</strong> – I think there's some kind of festival going on. Anyway, this is where we're getting out yacht properly fixed. It needs to be good enough for <strong>the next part of our journey</strong>. We've decided to sail in a straight line across the Pacific Ocean and then, well, we're taking <strong>a short cut</strong> through <strong>the Panama Canal</strong>. It's a long, long way so we need plenty of <strong>supplies</strong> … but there's <strong>a problem</strong>…</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>What's wrong Sophia? You look a bit worried.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Well I've got all our supplies – <strong>milk, water, bread, tea, bird food</strong> for <strong>the parrot</strong> – but I haven't got any money to pay for them. We left <strong>Sao Tome</strong> in such a rush that I didn't bring any.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Don't worry – here, use my credit card.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>They don't take <strong>credit cards</strong> here… just cash.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Oh really? I don't have much cash either – we could get some wired over to us or maybe Passepartout…</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Well don't look at me – I haven't got any cash – I've just used all my money to buy this <em>Savi</em> mask – isn't it beautiful? <strong>A real work of art.</strong> You need to collect one for your challenge, don't you?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>Yes I do - well done. Well, if we haven’t got any cash, we’ll have to sell some of our things. How about <strong>the parrot</strong>?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>We can't do that – I've given it <strong>a name</strong> – <strong>Peggy</strong>.</p>

 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Right, shall we take turns to work and sleep? This time, two people can stay on deck while one of us sleeps. <strong>The parrot</strong> can do what he wants. We don't want any more little accidents, do we Sophia?</p>

"<p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Day 7 – we're in the Cape Verde islands and, no, we didn't sink! We have made it to port.  <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>So there's an email from John who says… he hopes our trip is going well… and to remind me, that as part of the challenge, I have to bring back some rare, unusual souvenirs – and he wants a recording of some traditional music.  <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Phil, everything is fixed. I've filled up with drinking water. It didn't cost much and the chap who fixed it gave me this CD – something for us to listen to on the yacht.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>What is it?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>I don't know. It's just a CD of the local <em>Morna</em> music.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil</strong><br /><strong>What does it sound like?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>He said <strong>it's a bit like blues music</strong>. Have a listen.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil<br /></span></strong>That's brilliant Passepartout! What would I do without you?!</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Day 10 – and I'm out in the Atlantic Ocean – and what a big ocean it is when you look at it from our small yacht, The Mermaid. It is miles and miles of blue and grey water with nothing to see on the horizon. But we've got a good tail wind and we seem to be making good progress. Passepartout is at the wheel, steering our yacht to our next destination – St Helena. I'm helping out by making tea…</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Cup of tea, Passepartout?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>More tea! OK then, it will help me concentrate. The sea is getting quite rough and I need your help up here on deck…<strong>&nbsp;</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>RADIO MESSAGE:<br /></strong><em>Attention all shipping. A deep depression is forming in the South Atlantic, moving north. Severe gale force 11 winds are expected with heavy rain</em>. <em>Visibility will be poor.</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Strong wind. Heavy rain. Sounds nasty. We're going to have to change direction. Get your waterproof clothes on – we're in for a wet and bumpy ride…</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>The weather is already getting bad. The wind is very strong and the rain is hammering down and stinging our faces. Not my favourite weather – I prefer the calm, warm, sunny type. But we have no choice – we need to find shelter. Passepartout says we should go to some islands at 0.3 degrees north, 6.6 degrees east. Where could that be? And will we make it before the storm gets us? This was a dream trip – and suddenly <strong>it’s like a nightmare</strong></em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>Phil what are you doing? Hold onto that rope. Don't let go or we'll lose the sail.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>OK. It's getting very dark. Do you know which way to go?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Yes – of course I do – we do have a satellite navigation system. According to this, we're not too far from the coast – but I can't see anything.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil</strong></p> 
 <p>Look! I can see lights of Sao Tome. Is that a lighthouse? Is it a harbour?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Yes. I think it is… but I don't know how we're going to land in these stormy seas. We're just going to hit the rocks.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Hey look! There's someone on the harbour wall waving their arms. Let's get closer… Is it a mermaid?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP<br /></span></strong>A mermaid? She has legs.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Sophia<br /></span></strong>Over here. Quick! Throw me the rope.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil</strong>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /><em>Phew. What luck! We're on dry land, safe from the storm and it’s all thanks to the help of a woman who lives on the island. She's invited us to her house to dry off and warm up. &nbsp;But are we in the right place?</em></p> 
 <p><strong>Phil</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>Thanks so much for helping us – you saved our boat – and our lives.</p> 
 <p><strong>Sophia</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span>My name is Sophia. I'm happy to have helped. Here you are – try some bobofrito and a cup of hot chocolate.</p> 
 <p><strong>PP</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>Mmm, nice. <strong>They taste like banana</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Sophia</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>That's what they are – bobofrito is banana fried in coconut oil. Do you like it?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Do I like it? It’s amazing… just… let… me get some more… Mmmm…</p> 
 <p><strong>Sophia</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>So tell me, what are you guys doing here?</p> 
 <p><strong>PP</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>We're sailing round the world but we needed to shelter from the storm. We were heading for St Helena… is that right, Phil?</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>What? Oh yes, that's right. Sorry, I was enjoying this delicious hot chocolate. It tastes great too.</p> 
 <p><strong>Sophia</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>It's made with our finest cacao beans. It's what Sao Tome and Principe is famous for.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>Cacao beans! That's great because they are one of the things I have to collect as part of my challenge. Can I take some with me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Sophia</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>Your challenge?</p> 
 <p><strong>PP</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>Yes, we're sailing around the world from London back to London in 80 days. It's a stupid idea, isn't it?</p> 
 <p><strong>Sophia</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>Hmm, well maybe not. Actually, you can have a bag of these beans if you can do me a favour?</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>I'm sure we can help you.<strong>&nbsp;</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></strong><em>Sophia has told me she was also sailing around the world when she stopped in Sao Tome for a rest and ended up falling in love with a man who she then married. &nbsp;But her husband has started being cruel to her and she wants to leave the island and go home. Because she's got no money, she wants us to give her a lift back to Britain. The long way round! She is an experienced sailor, so how can we refuse? There is only one problem – we'll need to work out how she can escape without her husband noticing.&nbsp;This is exciting stuff!</em></p>

"<p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Hello again. It's Phil here. You may know that I've been set a challenge to sail around the world in 80 days – it's an impossible challenge especially as I have never sailed a yacht before. But I said 'yes' – so here it goes...</em>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>So, here we at Saint Catherine's Dock and look – here's my yacht <em>– The Mermaid</em> - I know she's a bit scruffy but I'm sure she'll get you round the world…</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Hmm, on my own! That's the bit that worries me. It's a very small boat.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>It's a yacht – not a boat – look: it's got a sail! Anyway, you'll be fine. Just call me on the satellite phone if you have any problems.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Hello, hi. Phil. Phil! It's me.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Pete, what are you doing here?</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<em>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</em><br /></strong><em>Pete is my office assistant: He makes the tea, he does the photocopying, he sometimes gives me ideas for my books. He's a great guy – so I'm really pleased to see him now…</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Tom posted a message on Facebook that you're going on a trip round the world, or something. I couldn't believe my eyes – so I had to come here and see for myself. Look, I've brought you some books to read… and a map – you'll find that useful.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>I will… but what I really need is a travelling companion… someone who can help me on my journey… someone like you?! How about it?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>No. Absolutely not. I can't. I've got to… errr… feed the cat.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>I'll feed your cat. Go on. Can't you see he needs your help!</p> 
 <p><strong>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</strong><br />I get<strong> seasick</strong>…</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Rubbish! I remember when you went sailing with your Dad – you were always fine.</p> 
 <p><strong>PP</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>That was different. We were sailing on a lake.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil</strong><span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span>Well, you know about sails and rope and anchors – you'd be great. Besides, if you come with me you can have a share of the money.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Tom &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>If you get home in 80 days!</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<em>&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</em><br /></strong><em>I'm pleased to report that Pete is joining me. I'm so pleased I have someone to 'show me the ropes', as it were – in other words, show me what to do. He's a good friend, a loyal assistant and he goes everywhere with me so I'm giving him the nickname 'Passepartout', just like in the original book, Around the World in Eighty Days – I hope he likes it!</em></p> 
 <p><strong>Phil&nbsp;<em>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</em><br /></strong><em>We've set sail. Our adventure has begun. Let me describe the yacht to you<strong>. </strong>It is 12 metres long. It has a huge mast, with the mainsail attached. There is an engine as well just in case there's no wind. The wooden deck has seating at the<strong> stern </strong>– that's the back.There are some steps down to the galley – that's the kitchen – and there are two <strong>berths</strong> or beds for us to sleep in. I can't believe we're going to live in this tiny space for 80 days!</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Phil, we've got the wind in our sails, we're making good progress. I can't even see land any more.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Yes. Thanks to you, it's <strong>plain sailing</strong>! So, what does this rope do?</p> 
 <p><strong>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</strong><br />It moves the<strong> jib</strong> – the sail at the front.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>And this one?</p> 
 <p><strong>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</strong><br />That moves the boom from side to side. No, no. But don't pull it until…</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Ouch! That hurt.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil&nbsp;<em>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</em><br /></strong><em>Day 5 and I'm learning how to sail but my best skills are in the galley, making tea. The weather is good but we seem to have a problem with the yacht…</em></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Passepartout, is it me or is it getting a bit wet down in the <strong>galley</strong>?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Let me have a look. Oh dear! There's water all over the floor. I think the boat is leaking.</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>What? What are we going to do?</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Drown!</p> 
 <p><strong><span>Phil &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br /></span></strong>What? Really? I'm going to get on the radio and call for help… Mayday! Mayday! Oh no. The radio isn't working. We're in big trouble!</p> 
 <p><strong><span>PP &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br /></span></strong>Be quiet. Calm down Phil. The radio isn't turned on – and we don't need to abandon ship just yet. I need to know where this water is coming from. It's only a slow leak but I think we need to fix it quickly. We need to head for dry land.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil&nbsp;<br /></strong><em>According to the map the nearest land is some islands at 16 degrees north, 24 degrees west. Do you know where that is? Let's hope we get there before we sink.</em></p>

"<p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Hello, I'm Phil.&nbsp;I live in London. My apartment is close to the Houses of Parliament and I can hear the bells of Big Ben chiming every hour. I live on bus route number 88 which is handy because it takes me to my office in Oxford Circus. What do I do? Well, I'm an author –&nbsp;I write books&nbsp;– but don't worry if you haven't heard of me, my books never sell – ever. In fact&nbsp;I want a career change&nbsp;because I desperately need some money. When I pay all my bills, you see, I only have enough spare money to buy a few drinks at my local pub – The Horse and Groom. That reminds me – I've got to go there now to meet some friends. Excuse me, we'll speak again soon.</em></p> 
 <p><strong>AT THE PUB</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>John<br /></strong>Hello Phil. Late again!</p> 
 <p><strong>Emily<br /></strong>Hello Phil.&nbsp;How is your writing going?</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>You know. It's all in my head not on paper.</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>Hi Phil, mate, how are you? We were just talking about travelling – Emily here, says she's climbed up Mount Everest! Rather extreme <strong>backpacking</strong>, don't you think?!</p> 
 <p><strong>Emily<br /></strong>I did do it. Five years ago. So come on John,&nbsp;what amazing thing have you done?</p> 
 <p><strong>John<br /></strong>Oh, I just went cycling across South America!</p> 
 <p><strong>Emily<br /></strong>You didn't!!</p> 
 <p><strong>John<br /></strong>I did. In my <strong>gap year</strong>. It was such a brilliant time. Four months on the road, although I did get a bit tired.</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>Sounds great. Did I ever tell you that I sailed across the Atlantic to America in a yacht I built with my own hands? I still have that yacht down at the docks – but I never use it now. How about you Phil –&nbsp;when did you have your big life <strong>adventure</strong>?</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>Oh me? I haven't done much really. I'm not really one for adventure.</p> 
 <p><strong>Emily<br /></strong>Why not?</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>Err… I never had any money - and&nbsp;where would I go?</p> 
 <p><strong>John<br /></strong>Come on, you need some adventure in your life.&nbsp;Don't you feel like doing some <strong>globetrotting</strong>?</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>Hey! I've got an idea!</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>Tom has come up with a crazy idea where I could make some money and have some adventure. He has offered to lend me his yacht to sail around the world! Yeah – mad isn't it?! He thinks I could write about my adventures and make some money from it. But… I'm not someone who takes risks and I can definitely think of some problems…</em></p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>Slight problem… I can't sail.</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>No problem. There's an app you can download. It'll show you everything.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>An app? I'll need more than that. I've never sailed a yacht in my life.</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>It's easy! And how about if I&nbsp;<em>give&nbsp;</em>you the boat – I'll never use it again - you can sell it when you get back. It'll earn you a fortune, on top of the money you get from your travel writing.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>I couldn't possibly keep your yacht. You might want to use it again one day.</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>Hmmm yes, that's true.</p> 
 <p><strong>John<br /></strong>I&nbsp;know.&nbsp;Why don't you make it into a challenge?</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>Yes, John! Great idea. I'll tell you what – I'll make you a bet.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>A&nbsp;bet – for money –&nbsp;what is it?</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>Do you remember that story by Jules Verne&nbsp;– when that guy, Phileas Fogg had to travel around the world in 80 days?</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>Yes.</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>Well, you've got to do it in 80 days. I bet you the boat that you won't do it. If you don't do it, I'll keep the boat.<em>&nbsp;If</em>&nbsp;you&nbsp;<em>do</em>&nbsp;sail around the world in 80 days, then you can keep the boat – and you can sell it if you want. He'll never do it!</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>Hold on.&nbsp;How much have you had to drink?&nbsp;You want me to sail around the world, on my own, in 80 days?! Impossible.</p> 
 <p><strong>Tom<br /></strong>I know. But if you want an adventure – and you want to keep the yacht – then that's the challenge. Exactly 80 days to sail all the way around the world – not a minute longer.</p> 
 <p><strong>Emily<br /></strong>Go on Phil, it'll be brilliant. Here, have another drink…</p> 
 <p><strong>John<br /></strong>Yes, and have my drink too.</p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong><em>What should I do?</em><em>&nbsp;It is true I need an adventure but this one is huge. I know, I'll have a few more drinks and think about it…</em></p> 
 <p><strong>Phil<br /></strong>OK. Yes - I accept the challenge!</p>
