"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>A lot has happened to Ebenezer Scrooge. How will this story end? Scrooge's only love used to be money, but now he might be a changed man! After the struggle with the frightening Spirit of Christmas Yet To Come, he found himself in his own bed, in his own room, and he felt happy and ready to change his life.</p> 
 <p><strong>AT SCROOGE'S HOUSE</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>I'm as light as a bird, I'm as happy as an angel, I'm as merry as a schoolboy, I'm as giddy as a drunken man. A merry Christmas to everybody! A happy New Year to all the world. Hello!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Scrooge ran to the window and put out his head. Bells are ringing! Ah! The sun was shining, the air felt fresh. Everything was wonderful!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Hey boy! Yes, you. Look up. Here in the window! What's today?</p> 
 <p><strong>Boy<br /></strong>It's Christmas Day, sir!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>It's Christmas Day. I haven't missed it. The Spirits have done it all in one night. Hello, my good boy. Do you know whether they've sold the special turkey that was hanging up there?</p> 
 <p><strong>Boy<br /></strong>What? The one as big as me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Yes! Go and buy it, and tell them to bring it here, so I may give them the address to take it to. Come back with the man, and I'll give you a little money. Come back with him in less than five minutes and I'll give you a lot of money.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The boy ran off as fast as he could.</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>I'll send it to Bob Cratchit's. He will not know who sends it. It's twice the size of Tiny Tim!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Then Scrooge went to the streets. He was greeting everyone: &quot;Merry Christmas! Merry Christmas!&quot; He approached the gentlemen who had asked him to help the poor. He had behaved so badly before, when he refused to give anything. But now, he offered them a generous donation.</p> 
 <p><strong>IN THE STREET</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Gentleman<br /></strong>My dear Mr Scrooge, are you serious?! I don't know what to say to such kindness!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>In the afternoon Scrooge went to his nephew's house for that dinner he was invited to but didn't want to go to. Do you remember that? How will his nephew react?</p> 
 <p><strong>AT SCROOGE'S NEPHEW'S HOUSE ENTRANCE</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge's Nephew<br /></strong>Who's that?! Uncle Scrooge! Welcome, uncle! Come and have some fun with us!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>His nephew received him with open arms. And what a party it was! It was great to be in that same party the Spirit of Christmas Present had shown him before. And this time everybody could see Scrooge and talk to him. The next morning, the old man went to the office very early to catch Bob Cratchit coming late. Eighteen and a half minutes late!</p> 
 <p><strong>AT SCROOGE'S OFFICE</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>What do you mean by coming here at this time of day?</p> 
 <p><strong>Bob Cratchit<br /></strong>I'm very sorry, sir. It's only once a year. It will not be repeated. I was making rather merry yesterday, you see, sir...</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Now, I'll tell you what, my friend: I am not going to stand this sort of thing any longer. And therefore… and therefore I'm about to raise your salary!</p> 
 <p><strong>Bob Cratchit<br /></strong>Mr Scrooge?!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>A Merry Christmas, Bob, my good friend. I'll raise your salary, and help your hard-working family, and we'll discuss your problems this very afternoon, over a Christmas drink!</p> 
 <p><strong>Bob Cratchit<br /></strong>Wonderful, Mr Scrooge! Wonderful!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Scrooge did it all, and much, much more. He became a second father to Tiny Tim, who did not die, and a good friend to all. Some people laughed to see how he'd changed, but he let them laugh. His own heart laughed: and that was quite enough for him. It was always said of Scrooge, that he knew how to keep the Christmas cheer alive and well. I hope we do the same. Tiny Tim has the last word:</p> 
 <p><strong>Tiny Tim<br /></strong>God bless us, everyone!</p> 
 "
"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Let's continue the story of Ebenezer Scrooge. The Spirit of Christmas Yet to Come couldn't have been more different from the Spirit of Christmas Present Scrooge had just seen disappearing. It was very tall and it was hidden in a black cape and hood. It didn't speak at all. Scrooge was getting used to the company of ghosts by now but he was afraid of this one.</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Ghost of the Future, I am more afraid of you than any spirit I've seen. But I know your purpose is to do me good. And I hope to become another man from the one I was, so I am prepared to be in your company. And do it with a thankful heart.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Was Scrooge really changing his ways? They went to the financial district and the Spirit stopped near a group of businessmen who were chatting.</p> 
 <p><strong>Businessman 1<br /></strong>I don't know much about it. I only know he's dead. It's likely to be a very cheap funeral! I'm certain I don't know of anybody who'll go to it. Should we volunteer?</p> 
 <p><strong>Businessman 2<br /></strong>I don't mind going if a lunch is provided! What happened to the money?</p> 
 <p><strong>Businessman 1<br /></strong>Well, he didn't give it to me!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Scrooge knew these men. But why did the Spirit make him listen to this conversation? No answer. Then the Spirit took him to a bad part of town. Criminals lived there. Some people were trying to sell stolen goods and they were making fun of the person who used to own them.</p> 
 <p><strong>Housekeeper<br /></strong>Who's the worse for the loss of a few things like these? Not a dead man, I suppose. He frightened everyone away from him when he was alive, but he profits us now he's dead!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And even the shirt the dead man was wearing was sold. A housekeeper, a laundress, an undertaker - they stood in line to make a profit on the dead man's things. Scrooge was shocked! He asked the Ghost to show him people with kindness towards the dead. And where do you think they went? Scrooge found himself back at Bob Cratchit's house. But this time everybody was sad and quiet. Bob Cratchit had just returned from church where he had made arrangements for somebody's funeral.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mrs Cratchit<br /></strong>How was it, Robert?</p> 
 <p><strong>Bob Cratchit<br /></strong>I wish you could have been there, dear wife. It would have done you good to see how green a place it is. But you'll see it often. I promised him that I would walk there on a Sunday. My little, little child...</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Scrooge knew now that Tiny Tim was dead. But who was that man whose death others were talking about? The Spirit of Christmas Yet to Come took Scrooge to a graveyard and pointed ahead. On the stone of a neglected grave, the old man read a name: Ebenezer Scrooge! It was his own name! It was Scrooge's grave!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>No, Spirit. Oh no, no! Spirit, hear me. I'm not the man I was. Why show me this, if all hope is gone?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Wow! That's a brand new Scrooge we're seeing! And he's not done yet in his pleading...</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Good Spirit, tell me that I still may change these shadows you have shown me, by changing my life. I will celebrate Christmas in my heart, and try to keep it all the year. I'll live in the Past, the Present, and the Future. The Spirits of all Three shall live within me. I will not shut out the lessons that they teach. Oh, tell me that I may remove the writing on this stone!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Scrooge grabbed the Spirit's hand. The Spirit tried to free itself. In the end, it just disappeared. Scrooge found himself grabbing his own bedpost. What will happen now? I'll tell you next time.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Ebenezer Scrooge woke up just before the clock struck one again. He was ready for the Spirit of Christmas Present. This time, he met his guide in the next room, which looked very different from usual. It was decorated with holly and other plants. On the table, there was a lot of delicious Christmas food like turkey, cake, fruit... Scrooge talked to the ghost.</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Spirit, take me where you like. Last night I learnt a lesson. Tonight, if you want to teach me, let me profit by it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Oh, that's not the Scrooge we knew before. No longer arrogant?! Well, the Spirit took Scrooge to the edge of the city where his clerk Bob Cratchit lived. The man entered his humble home carrying a little boy who had a crutch and iron around his legs. His wife was preparing the meal.</p> 
 <p><strong>AT BOB CRATCHIT'S HOUSE</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Mrs Cratchit<br /></strong>How did Tiny Tim behave at church, Robert?</p> 
 <p><strong>Bob Cratchit<br /></strong>As good as gold! He told me on our way home that he hoped that people noticed him in the church, because he's disabled. It might be good for them to remember on Christmas Day our Lord, who made lame people walk and blind men see.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Tiny Tim was a sweet little boy who knew the meaning of Christmas. But he was very sick. Scrooge felt sorry for him and asked the Spirit what was going to happen.</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Spirit, tell me if Tiny Tim will live.</p> 
 <p><strong>Spirit of Christmas Present<br /></strong>I see an empty seat in the corner, and a crutch without an owner. If things don't change in the future, the child will die.</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>No, no. Oh, no, kind Spirit. Say he'll live!</p> 
 <p><strong>Spirit of Christmas Present<br /></strong>If he's going to die, he should do it, and&nbsp;<em>decrease the surplus population.</em></p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>These words caused a huge and sudden feeling of deep regret in Scrooge's heart. That was exactly what he had said earlier to the gentlemen who had asked for a donation to help the poor. If the poor died&nbsp;<em>it would be good to help decrease the surplus population</em>. Then, Scrooge heard Cratchit mention his name...</p> 
 <p><strong>Bob Cratchit<br /></strong>After this wonderful dinner, let's raise our glasses. A Merry Christmas to us all, my dears! God bless us! And also Mr Scrooge, the Father of the Feast! Come on, dear wife!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mrs Cratchit<br /></strong>I wish I had him here, Robert. I'd give him a piece of my mind! Such a horrible, hard, unfeeling man, Mr Scrooge. I'll drink to his health because it is Christmas, but not because of him.</p> 
 <p><strong>Tiny Tim<br /></strong>God bless us every one!</p> 
 <p><strong>Bob Cratchit<br /></strong>Thank you, Tim, my dear child.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>There was no doubt Scrooge was the monster of the family. But if the thought of her husband's selfish boss annoyed Mrs Cratchit, it caused laughter elsewhere. The Ghost of Christmas Present took Scrooge to his nephew's house - to the Christmas dinner the old man had refused to go to.</p> 
 <p><strong>AT SCROOGE'S NEPHEW'S HOUSE</strong>&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge's Nephew<br /></strong>...and my uncle said that Christmas was a humbug! He's a funny man, that's the truth. And not as pleasant as he could be. However, his crimes carry their own price. His money is of no use to him. He doesn't do any good with it. He doesn't make himself comfortable with it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The house was full of people dancing, playing games. The Spirit noticed that Scrooge was enjoying himself. The night was coming to an end when Scrooge saw two figures at the ghost's feet. What were they? They looked like children, but they were old and frightening. Scrooge was shocked.</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>I'm sorry to ask but... are they yours?&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Spirit of Christmas Present<br /></strong>They are Man's creatures. The boy is Ignorance. The girl is Want. Be afraid of them both, but most of all you should fear this boy for on his face I see a terrible destiny!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Don't they have a place to go?</p> 
 <p><strong>Spirit of Christmas Present<br /></strong><em>Are there no prisons? Are there no workhouses?</em></p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Yes, once more Scrooge had his own words repeated back to him. He had always thought the poor&nbsp;<em>had prisons and workhouses to go to</em>, hadn't he? Eat your words, Mr Scrooge! Well, the bell struck twelve and that was it for the Ghost of Christmas Present. He disappeared. But the third spirit was coming. You'll hear about it next time.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Let's continue the story of Ebenezer Scrooge, the selfish man who didn't like Christmas. Scrooge was in bed when the curtains were opened and he saw a face...</p> 
 <p><strong>Spirit of Christmas Past<br /></strong>I'm the Ghost of Christmas Past - your past. Come with me.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The Spirit took Scrooge through a wall and suddenly they found themselves on an open country road. The city had disappeared. Scrooge was very excited.</p> 
 <p><strong>IN SCROOGE'S OLD NEIGHBOURHOOD</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Good heavens! I grew up in this place. That's the river! And... Oh, and I used to climb that tree…</p>

 <p><strong>Spirit of Christmas Past<br /></strong>Your sister... She had a big heart! She died when she was an adult and had, I think, children. Your nephew!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Yes. She was so kind...</p>

 <p><strong>Mr Fezziwig<br /></strong>Yo ho ho boys, no more work tonight. It's Christmas Eve! Clear away my lads, and let's have lots of room here!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The warehouse was transformed into a bright ballroom in no time at all. In came a musician, Mrs Fezziwig and her three daughters, and all the young men and women employed in the business. It got old Scrooge thinking. He told the Spirit...</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Mr Fezziwig had the power to make us happy or unhappy; to make our work easy or hard; pleasure or pain. The happiness he gave us is as great as if it had cost a huge pile of gold. I should like to be able to say a word or two to my clerk Bob Cratchit just now<strong>.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Is there a change in old Scrooge? Mmmm... Maybe... Well, the mood was darker when the Spirit took Scrooge to see another Christmas a few years later. Then, the young Scrooge was starting to look obsessed with money. He wasn't alone. There was a young woman by his side. Oh, she was crying...</p> 
 <p><strong>IN THE PAST</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge's girlfriend<br /></strong>Something else has taken my place; if it can cheer and comfort you as I wanted to do, I have no reason to cry. May you be happy in the life you have chosen!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Spirit, show me no more. Take me home. Why do you torture me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>It was hard for Scrooge to see how his girlfriend left him when he started to fall in love with money. But the Spirit's work wasn't done yet. He took Scrooge to yet another Christmas a few years from then. And the greedy, old man saw her happy with a husband and children - children who he almost wished were his own. Scrooge was very depressed when he got back home: the kind sister whose son he rejected, the generous employer, the lost girlfriend – that's a lot to take in! But there were still two spirits left. What would the Spirit of Christmas Present show Scrooge? Let's see it tomorrow. I can't wait!</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>This is the story of Ebenezer Scrooge, a man who loved money and didn't like Christmas. There he was, on Christmas Eve, in his office. He was keeping an eye on his clerk Bob Cratchit. Scrooge wanted to get every little bit of work from Cratchit before allowing him to spend Christmas Day at home. Scrooge thought Christmas was a waste of time! Even his nephew couldn't convince him that it wasn't.&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>IN SCROOGE'S OFFICE</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge's Nephew<br /></strong>A Merry Christmas, uncle!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Bah! Humbug!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge's Nephew<br /></strong>You don't mean that, I'm sure!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>What's Christmas time to you but a time for paying bills without money? You find yourself a year older, but not an hour richer! What good has it ever done you?</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge's Nephew<br /></strong>I've always thought of Christmas as a kind, forgiving, charitable, pleasant time. A time when men and women seem to open their hearts freely. It's never put money in my pocket, but I believe that it's done me good!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Humbug!</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge's Nephew<br /></strong>Come on, uncle, come and have dinner with us tomorrow.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Scrooge's nephew was persistent but the old man wouldn't change his mind. He was in his usual bad mood when two gentlemen came to his office to ask for a donation to offer Christmas dinner to the poor. Scrooge worked in the money-lending business. No donation from him...</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Gentlemen, are there no prisons and workhouses, where the poor receive food and accommodation in return for some work?</p> 
 <p><strong>Gentleman<br /></strong>We wish we could say there aren't any, Mr Scrooge. Many poor people would rather die than go to prison or the...</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>They should die and decrease the surplus population. And... well, it's none of my business anyway. They cost a lot of money, and the poor should go there. Goodbye, sir.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Typical Scrooge! He feels sorry for no-one, helps no-one. With him, it's all about money. He thought of nothing else. His partner, Jacob Marley, had died seven years before, at Christmas. Marley was like Scrooge when he was alive. But now he was gone. Or was he?</p> 
 <p><strong>AT SCROOGE'S HOUSE</strong><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Who's there? I'm finally home and I want some peace!</p> 
 <p><strong>Marley<br /></strong>Scroooge... Scrooooooge...</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>What is this? A ghost?! It's not possible! I must be having indigestion and seeing things that aren't there!</p> 
 <p><strong>Marley<br /></strong>Scrooge. In life I was your partner, Jacob Marley.</p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Marley, is it really you?! And what is this strange metal chain you are wearing? It's made of cash-boxes, keys, locks, heavy purses...</p> 
 <p><strong>Marley<br /></strong>I wear the chain I made in life. Of my own free will I wore it when I was alive. Is its pattern strange to you? Or do you wish to know the weight and length of the heavy chain you are carrying yourself?<strong>&nbsp;</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Scrooge<br /></strong>Don't say that, Jacob. And why is this happening to you? You were always a good man of business…</p> 
 <p><strong>Marley<br /></strong>Business!? Mankind was my business. Charity, kindness - were all my business. Why did I walk through crowds of people with my eyes turned down? I'm here to warn you, that you still have a chance of escaping my fate. You'll be visited by three spirits. Expect the first spirit tomorrow at one o'clock in the morning. And remember what I've told you.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Marley disappeared into the night, flying out of an open window with other ghosts which looked as miserable as him. Scrooge was shocked. I'll tell you about the visit of the first spirit next time.</p>

"<p><strong>Scene 1 – A cat and his man</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>NARRATOR<br /></strong>We present: The story of Dick Whittington and his cat, a pantomime.&nbsp;Featuring the cats and cast of BBC Learning English. Let's start off by meeting our hero, Dick Whittington. He's just walking home after a long day at the office… Hey there Dick.</p> 
 <p><strong>DICK<br /></strong>Hello!</p>

 <p><strong>APPLE<br /></strong>I've never seen this man before in my life.</p> 
 <p><strong>DICK<br /></strong>How can you say that? I'm your oldest friend. Come on, let's go out to celebrate. I'll get you that nice tuna steak I promised.</p> 
 <p><strong>APPLE<br /></strong>Oh you're all friendly now, now that you're about to become Lord Mayor of London. Where were you when I needed you? Getting cosy with Princess over there, <strong>no doubt</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>DICK<br /></strong>Ah yes, Apple. I want you to meet Snow White.</p> 
 <p><strong>SNOW<br /></strong>Hello Apple. I've heard all about you.</p> 
 <p><strong>APPLE<br /></strong>I'm sure you have.</p> 
 <p><strong>FULBRIGHT<br /></strong>Look, I really need to get home. Is he your owner or not?</p> 
 <p><strong>APPLE<br /></strong>Maybe. Oh all right. Yes, he's my owner.</p> 
 <p><strong>DICK<br /></strong>Oh Apple, thank you! I'll never forget this!</p> 
 <p><strong>FULBRIGHT<br /></strong>Dick Whittington, I hereby pronounce you Lord&nbsp;Mayor of London!</p> 
 <p><strong>NARRATOR<br /></strong>And so, the Lord Mayor's carriage makes its way slowly down Oxford Street, surrounded by crowds of rats, cats and people. What a fine summer's day to have a Lord-Mayor-making-celebration. Yes and what a fine young man this Richard Whittington is. Let's just hope he's got enough <strong>spunk </strong>for this most difficult and challenging job. There are so many things that a Lord Mayor has to do… he has to ensure that Big Ben is fed twice a day, and that all tourists pronounce the word 'Greenwich' correctly and of course his most important job of all is to make sure that the entire city of London never, ever runs out of paperclips…</p> 
 <p><strong>DICK<br /></strong>What's that you say? Paperclips! I thought I <strong>was finished with </strong>all that! Oh well, at least as Lord Mayor of London I'll be able to marry Snow White.</p> 
 <p><strong>SNOW<br /></strong>What's that you say? Marry you! I said I'd <strong>go out with </strong>you, but no one ever mentioned the big white dress! <strong>One step at a time</strong>, Lord Mayor!</p> 
 <p><strong>DICK<br /></strong>OK, OK… one step at a time. But…you will go out with me, won't you?</p> 
 <p><strong>SNOW<br /></strong>On a trial basis – OK. I'll go out with you.</p> 
 <p><strong>NARRATOR<br /></strong>And so they might not be <strong>happy ever after</strong>, but let's hope our friends Dick Whittington, his cat Apple and Snow White will be moderately content for a good amount of time… The End. Dick Whittington was played by Jackie Dalton, Apple by William Kremer; Neil Edgeller was Franky Banky; Snow White was played by Elena Newton and Amber Barnfather was Tigger. "<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. Alice has had lots of adventures in Wonderland. Now, she has been called as a witness in the trial of the Knave of Hearts. The King of Hearts is the judge, but Alice has grown so tall that her head reaches the top of the courthouse and all the people seem very far away.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>How small you all are!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>The witness must come to the witness box!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice jumped up and knocked over the jury box. It was full of animals and they all fell out.</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>Ooh, ow, oh are you hurt? Excuse me, is that my chair? Etc...</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'm so sorry!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>What do you know about this business?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Nothing at all!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The King looked in his Book of&nbsp;<strong>Rules</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Rule forty-two. &quot;All&nbsp;<strong>persons</strong>&nbsp;more than a mile high must leave the court.&quot;</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'm not a mile high!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Indeed you are not! You are nearly two miles high!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Well, I'm not going! And&nbsp;<strong>you can't make</strong>&nbsp;me!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice had grown a little bit more, and the King, who was now the size of Alice's shoe,&nbsp;<strong>could see</strong>&nbsp;she was right about that part. His face went very&nbsp;<strong>pale</strong>&nbsp;and he closed&nbsp;his Book of Rules.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>White Rabbit. Ask the jury: what is their decision about this matter? Did the Knave steal the Queen's tarts?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>But there was more&nbsp;<strong>evidence.</strong>&nbsp;The White Rabbit gave a letter to the King, who opened it and turned to the Knave of Hearts.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Knave of Hearts, did you write this?</p> 
 <p><strong>Knave of Hearts<br /></strong>I didn't write it! Look at the end of it: there is no name written there!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Then you are not a honest man! An honest man always signs his work! Read the letter!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And the White Rabbit read the letter. No-one understood a single word of it.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>That's the most important evidence we've heard today!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I don't believe there's any meaning in it!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>If there's no meaning in it, then we don't need to try to find any! Jury, what is your decision?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The Queen stamped her feet.</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>No, no no!&nbsp;<strong>Punishment</strong>&nbsp;first, decision afterwards!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>That's nonsense! The punishment comes last!</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Be quiet!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I won't!</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Off with her head!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>No-one moved. Alice realised she had grown to her full size.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Who cares about you? All of you!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice looked down at the little people all around her. She suddenly realised…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>You're nothing but a pack of cards!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>As soon as she said this, the animals, the birds, the King and Queen and everyone else turned into a pack of cards and they all flew up into the air and came flying down upon her. The cards fluttered and flew all around her head and shoulders and Alice gave a scream as she tried to beat them off with her hands…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ohhhh!!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And then another strange thing happened to Alice. She found herself back on the riverbank where our story began. She opened her eyes and saw her sister smiling at her.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice's sister<br /></strong>Wake up, Alice dear! What a long sleep you've had!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice's sister gently brushed away some dead leaves that had fallen from the tree and onto her face.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh… I've had such a curious dream.&nbsp;There was a White Rabbit and … I got bigger and smaller … and I met a caterpillar and a Hatter … and played croquet and … a cat that smiled and … so many things.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice told her sister all about the Wonderland in her dream and the adventures she had had there. Perhaps one day Alice will dream herself back to Wonderland. If she does, I'll be sure to tell you. Goodbye.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. Alice is having lots adventures in Wonderland. Now, she's in a courtroom full of animals. Everybody is waiting for the trial to start. The Queen and the King of Hearts have already arrived and they are sitting on their <strong>thrones</strong>. &nbsp;The rest of the room was filled with birds and animals and the whole pack of playing-card people. Alice saw the White Rabbit. He was holding a <strong>trumpet </strong>in one handand alarge piece of paper in the other. The White Rabbit blew the trumpet.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Silence in the court!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The trial started. The King was the <strong>judge</strong> and twelve animals were the <strong>jury</strong>. The King spoke first.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Read the accusation!</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>The Queen of Hearts, she made some <strong>tarts</strong>,<br />All on a summer day.<br />The Knave of Hearts, he stole those tarts<br />And took them quite away.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Knave of Hearts, what do you say?</p> 
 <p><strong>Knave of Hearts<br /></strong>It wasn't me! I didn't do it!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Silence! Call the first <strong>witness</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Bring in the first witness!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The first witness was the Hatter. He looked very <strong>nervous</strong>. He came into the court with a cup of tea in one shaking hand and a piece of bread and butter in the other.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Give your evidence Hatter, and don't be nervous, or you'll lose your head!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The King's words made the Hatter even more frightened. He was so confused and that he took a large bite out of his teacup instead of his bread and butter.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter<br /></strong>I'm a poor man, your Majesty.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>You're a very poor speaker.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Poor Hatter. He didn't use to be mad, you know. He used to be quite normal.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>And I used to be taller…</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice began to have a curious feeling. It was a feeling she remembered.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ohh.. I'm growing again!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>No-one noticed that Alice was getting taller. They were all watching the Hatter, who was too frightened to speak.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>You may go. Call the next witness!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The next witness was the cook.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Cook, what are tarts made of?</p> 
 <p><strong>Cook<br /></strong>Pepper, mostly.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Everybody started sneezing. Nobody seemed to notice Alice growing taller and taller. By the time they stopped sneezing, the cook had disappeared.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Never mind! Call the next witness!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice watched as the White Rabbit studied the piece of paper, looking for the name of the next witness. Imagine her surprise when he straightened up, took a deep breath and shouted the name of the next witness…</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Alice!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Everybody in the courtroom turned to look at Alice. Alice felt herself grow a little taller, as she took a deep breath, and stepped forward. Next time, I'll tell you what happened when Alice gives her evidence and the White Rabbit reads a letter from the Knave of Hearts. Curiouser and curiouser… Goodbye.&nbsp;</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello! After all her adventures, Alice has finally found the beautiful garden she's been looking for all this time. It's full of beautiful white roses. Alice wandered through the flowers until she saw a gardener. He was doing something very strange...</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Why are you painting the roses red?</p> 
 <p><strong>Gardener<br /></strong>The Queen - she wants red roses and I put white roses in by mistake. If the Queen finds them, she'll cut my head off! Oh no! Here comes the Queen!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The gardener threw himself to the ground and lay with his face down. A line of&nbsp;<strong>soldiers</strong>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<strong>courtiers</strong>&nbsp;came marching into the rose garden. They didn't look like people at all. They looked exactly like playing cards: their bodies were square and flat with their heads at the top and their hands and feet in the four corners. First came a group of ten soldiers, who were decorated with black clubs, then came ten of the Queen's servants, who were covered in red diamonds. Then came all the princes and princesses, wearing red hearts. The&nbsp;<strong>Knave of Hearts</strong>&nbsp;was carrying a crown on a cushion, and last of all came the King and Queen of Hearts. When they got to Alice, everybody stopped. The Queen looked at Alice.</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Who is this?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'm Alice,&nbsp;<strong>Your Majesty.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Can you play croquet?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Yes!</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Come on then! Everyone get to your places!</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>I'm over here... Are you over there? This is place, no this is your place, are we ready?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Everyone began running in different directions until they got into place and the game began. It was a very curious game: everything seemed to be alive! The balls were&nbsp;<strong>hedgehogs</strong>&nbsp;and the croquet mallets were&nbsp;<strong>flamingos</strong>. All the playing-card-soldiers bent over so they looked like&nbsp;<strong>arches</strong>. The players had to catch the flamingos first, which wasn't easy because they kept flying away. When the flamingos were caught, each player held their flamingo tightly under one arm, with the long neck and head hanging down to the ground. Then the hedgehogs curled up into spiky balls – and the players used the flamingos' heads to hit the hedgehogs so that they rolled through the playing-card soldier arches.</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>Is it my turn? Oh good shot! Have another go... oh do stand still! Very nicely played, it's your turn again, very good, etc...</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>What a curious game! I suppose I should play.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>It was a very curious game! There didn't seem to be any rules. Everyone played at the same time and the hedgehogs kept running away. Alice took a flamingo and tried to hit a hedgehog with it. But the flamingo moved its head and she missed. Soon the players began arguing and fighting for the hedgehogs and the Queen went around stamping her feet and shouting at everyone.</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Off with your head! Off with her head!</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals</strong><br />No it isn't your turn! That's my ball, give me my hedgehog! It's my turn, not yours! Is that my flamingo? That's cheating!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>How&nbsp;<strong>will I get out</strong>&nbsp;of here?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>As Alice was looking around for a way to escape, suddenly the Cheshire-Cat appeared in the air. He wasn't sitting on anything, he was just floating.</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>Are you enjoying the croquet?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>No. I don't think they play fairly at all. Everyone is arguing and there aren't any rules.</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>How do you like the Queen?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Not at all! I suppose I should try to play or&nbsp;<strong>she might cut off my head</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice went to find her hedgehog. She found it having a fight with another one. While she was trying to pull the two animals apart, her flamingo flew away.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh dear! I'm not doing very well at this game.&nbsp;<strong>What will the Queen think</strong>?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice was right to worry. Most of the other players had made the Queen angry for one reason or another and the soldiers took them away one by one. Soon there were only the King, the Queen and Alice left in the game. The Queen turned to Alice.</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>You! Come here! Who were you talking to?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>If you please, your Majesty...</p> 
 <p><strong>Voice<br /></strong>The&nbsp;<strong>trial&nbsp;</strong>is starting! The&nbsp;<strong>trial&nbsp;</strong>is starting!</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>The trial! Oh good! I love trials! Come along!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice had no choice but to follow the Queen. We'll leave her there for now. Next time. I'll tell you all about the Knave of Hearts, the stolen jam tarts and what happened when Alice met the Hatter and The White Rabbit again. Goodbye.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Hello! Alice is trying to find her way back to the beautiful garden she saw when she first arrived in Wonderland. On her way, she met the Cheshire-Cat in the woods, who told Alice about the March Hare and the Hatter. Alice found the March Hare and the Hatter, having a tea-party.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter and March Hare</strong><br />Would you like some tea? Tea? Yes please, and cake? One cake... two cakes? One lump or two?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />Curiouser and curiouser. They're having a tea-party. But where are all the guests?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />The Hatter and the March Hare were sitting at one end of a very long table, which had empty cups and plates all the way along it. But the only other guest was a mouse, who was sound asleep. Alice decided to join them.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter and March Hare</strong><br />No room here! I'm sorry, no room!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />There's plenty of room!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Alice sat down. The Hatter opened his eyes very wide.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter</strong><br />Why is a raven like a writing desk?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />Ooh, good. Riddles! I love riddles!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />The March Hare looked at Alice.</p> 
 <p><strong>March Hare</strong><br />You mean you know the answer, don't you?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />Yes, I do.</p> 
 <p><strong>March Hare</strong><br />Then you should say what you mean!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />I do. At least, I mean what I say. That's the same thing, isn't it?</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter</strong><br />But why is a raven like a writing-desk? Have you guessed the answer yet?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />No. I give up. What's the answer?</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter</strong><br />I don't know! Do you know?</p> 
 <p><strong>March Hare</strong><br />I don't know either!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />I think you should only ask riddles if you know the answer.</p> 
 <p><strong>March Hare</strong><br />Have some more tea.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />I haven't had any tea, have I? So I can't take more.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter</strong><br />You mean you can't take less. It's very easy to take more than nothing.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Alice got up and walked off without saying goodbye.</p> 
 <p><strong>March Hare</strong><br />More tea, Hatter?</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter</strong><br />Don't mind if I do!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />The Hatter and the March Hare didn't seem to notice her leaving. Alice went back into the woods. She looked back as she walked away. The Hatter and the March Hare were trying to put the mouse into the teapot.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter and Hare</strong><br />Mousey mousey! In you go! Plop! Oh, he does wriggle so. More tea?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />I'll never go there again! That was the stupidest tea-party I've ever been to in all my life!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Back in the woods, Alice saw a tree with a door in it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />That's very curious! I wonder what could be behind a door in a tree...</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />In Wonderland anything can be behind any door. Alice opened the door and there she was at the beginning of her adventures again – in the hall with the locked doors and the table with the little key on it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />I remember that little door and the key! This time I know what to do! I'm finally going to get into the garden!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Alice had learned a lot about growing and shrinking in Wonderland. She took the key off the table first… and then ate some of the mushroom she had taken from the caterpillar and put in her pocket. Soon she was small enough to unlock the door and go through it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />Oh, it's so pretty here!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />We'll leave Alice here for now, happy in the garden at last. Soon, she's going to meet the Queen and play croquet. Will she still be happy then? I'll tell you next time.</p>

 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I wonder who could live in such a little house!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Before she had the chance to wonder for very long,&nbsp;<strong>a fish ran&nbsp;</strong>out of the woods and knocked on the door.  <p><strong>Footman<br /></strong>From the Queen. An invitation for the Duchess to play&nbsp;<strong>croquet</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>The Duchess!!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice was so curious<strong>&nbsp;she went</strong>&nbsp;to knock on the door.  <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>It was easy to decide what to do with a pig. Alice took it outside and let it go into the woods.&nbsp;<strong>The Cheshire-Cat sat</strong>&nbsp;in a tree and watched her.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Cheshire-Cat, could you tell me which way I should go?</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>A Hatter lives over here, and a March Hare lives over there. They're both&nbsp;<strong>mad</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>But I don't want to meet mad people.</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>Oh, we're all mad here. Are you playing croquet with the Queen today?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'd love to play croquet with the Queen… but&nbsp;<strong>she hasn't invited me</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>You'll see me there…</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>After Alice frightened everyone by growing as big as a house, she ate some little cakes and&nbsp;<strong>shrank</strong>&nbsp;again. She&nbsp;doesn't like&nbsp;being so tiny, so she's looking for something to make her grow to the right size. But this is Wonderland and what she finds, sitting on top of a mushroom, is very curious indeed…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Am I as small as a mushroom, or is the mushroom as tall as me? Ohh!!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Sitting on top of the mushroom was a blue caterpillar smoking a&nbsp;<strong>hookah pipe.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>Who are you?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I… I'm not sure.&nbsp;I know&nbsp;who I was when I woke up this morning. But I've changed so many times since then!</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>What do you mean by that? Explain yourself!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I can't explain myself because I'm not myself. It's very confusing…<strong>&nbsp;</strong>I think&nbsp;you should tell me who YOU are first.</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>Why?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ummm…</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice couldn't think of any good reason. She decided to leave.</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>Come back! I have something important to say!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Yes?&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>Don't be unhappy.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Is that all?</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>No. So you think you've changed, do you?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I have, sir. I don't stay the same size for more than ten minutes!</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>What size do you want to be?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh,&nbsp;I don't mind. A little bit bigger is all I would like. Seven centimetres is such a terrible&nbsp;<strong>height</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>It is a very good height! I myself am exactly seven centimetres in height!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And with that, the caterpillar crawled off the mushroom and away.</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>One side of the mushroom will make you grow taller. The other side will make you grow shorter. Seven centimetres indeed!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Hmmm… let me pull this side… and now this side…But which side is which?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>There was only one way to find out the answer to that question. Alice took a bite of one piece of the mushroom - and shrank so quickly that she hit her&nbsp;<strong>chin</strong>&nbsp;on her foot.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />Ouch!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Quickly, she ate some of the other piece of mushroom and …</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Where have my&nbsp;<strong>shoulders</strong>&nbsp;gone? And my hands – where are you, hands?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice grew and grew until her&nbsp;<strong>neck</strong>&nbsp;was as long as a snake. Up and up she grew, through the branches and leaves, until her head was higher than the trees. Alice found she could move her neck just like a snake, bending this way and that. She was about to use her long neck to push her head down into the trees&nbsp;and look for her shoulders and hands, when suddenly a furious bird flew at her.</p> 
 <p><strong>Bird<br /></strong>Snake! Snake!&nbsp;You want&nbsp;my eggs!&nbsp;I know!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'm not a snake! I'm a… I'm a little girl!</p> 
 <p><strong>Bird<br /></strong>Little girl or snake, it doesn't matter to me, you want my eggs just the same!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I don't want your eggs, really I don't!</p> 
 <p><strong>Bird<br /></strong>Then be off with you! Go away!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The bird settled angrily into its nest. Alice ate a little of one side of the mushroom, then a little of the other, then a little of the first again until she was a good size. She decided to find her way back to the door to the beautiful garden that she saw when she first arrived in Wonderland. As she walked through the forest she found a little clearing, with a small house in it, not much more than a metre or so high.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I wonder who lives here? The house is so small – anyone who lives here will surely be afraid of me!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice ate a little more of the mushroom and quickly brought herself down to the right size for this little house. Next time, Alice meets a walking fish, talks to a smiling cat and has to look after a baby. Goodbye.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. Alice fell down a Rabbit Hole one day and found herself in a Wonderland, where animals talk, curious things happen and everything she eats and drinks makes her grow bigger or smaller. Now she is sitting alone. Suddenly, she heard footsteps. The White Rabbit was running towards her. He seemed to be very worried.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Oh dear! Where can I have dropped them? I must find them, or I'm sure The Duchess will <strong>chop</strong> <strong>off</strong> my head!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice guessed he was looking for the gloves and fan that he had dropped - but she didn't know where they were either. After all her growing and shrinking, Alice was exactly the same size as the rabbit. When the White Rabbit saw Alice, he spoke to her quite angrily.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Mary Ann! What are you doing out here? Run home this minute and get me a pair of gloves and a fan! Quickly!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>How surprised he'll be when he finds out I'm not Mary Ann!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong></p> 
 <p>Alice began to run, as the White Rabbit had told her, although she didn't quite know where she should run to. But soon, a little house appeared with the words 'W. Rabbit' written on the door.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I won't knock on the door. The real Mary Ann might hear me.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice crept into the house and went quietly upstairs to a little bedroom… and there she found two fans, three pairs of gloves and…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Another bottle! I hope it makes me grow bigger again. I'm tired of being such a tiny little thing!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>…and sure enough, Alice began to grow. Taller and taller she grew, until…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ouch! My head! That's quite tall enough. That's tall enough! O-o-o-oh…</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice tried her hardest to stop growing - but it seemed to her like the harder she tried, the taller she grew. Soon Alice was so big that she filled the whole room. Her head pressed up against the ceiling, her arm went out of the window, and one of her feet went up the <strong>chimney</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>What will become of me now?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Outside the house, a crowd started to gather. Alice heard voices.</p> 
 <p><strong>Voices<br /></strong>Oh my, whatever could it be? What’s that?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Soon, the White Rabbit arrived.</p> 
 <p><strong>White</strong> <strong>Rabbit<br /></strong>What's that in the window?</p> 
 <p><strong>Voice<br /></strong>It's an arm, sir!</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>An arm? Well, it's got no business being there! Bill! Bill! Fetch the <strong>ladder</strong> and take it away!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Bill was the <strong>gardener</strong>. He brought a ladder and climbed up on to the <strong>roof</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>I won't have an arm in my bedroom! Down you go Bill, down the chimney!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Poor Bill went up the ladder and tried to go down the chimney. But Alice's foot was waiting for him… with a big kick.</p> 
 <p><strong>Bill<br /></strong>Ohhhhhhhh!!!!</p> 
 <p><strong>Voices<br /></strong>Quick, quick, help him, help him up. Give him some air…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>There! That's got rid of him! Now what will they try?</p> 
 <p><strong>Voices<br /></strong>Cakes! Cakes! Try the cakes!</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Yes! The cakes: bring the cakes! We'll need a lot of them. That's right. Now, everybody, throw them through the other window!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>What's this…? Oh! Lots and lots of little cakes. &nbsp;I wonder… If I ate them, would I shrink again? They must do something… and I must get out of this house. I'll try just one of them to start with.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice ate one of the little cakes, and soon found herself to be a little smaller. She ate another and another, until at last she was just the right size to run out of the bedroom… and out of the house.</p> 
 <p><strong>Voices<br /></strong>Look! There she is! Get her! Catch her, quickly!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>But Alice was too fast for them. She ran far away from the White Rabbit's house, deeper and deeper into the forest until she became quite lost. She was wondering what she could eat or drink to make her grow to the right size again, when suddenly, she saw in front of her a large mushroom - about the same size as herself, with a large blue <strong>caterpillar</strong> sitting on top of it, smoking a pipe and taking no notice of Alice at all. Will the caterpillar help Alice to grow again? I'll tell you next time.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. So far, Alice had been very small, then very tall, then very small again in this strange Wonderland she found when she chased a talking rabbit and fell down the rabbit hole. Now she was swimming in a pool of her own tears, wondering what was going to happen next.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ooh, whatever's this? It's a mouse! Hello mouse! You're a very big mouse… but then, I'm a very, very little girl today. Whatever next?&nbsp;<strong>If this mouse talks, I won't be at all surprised</strong>… Oh Mouse, do you know the way out of this pool? I'm very tired of swimming about here, Mouse! Mouse? Hmmm. Perhaps it doesn't understand English. Maybe it's a French mouse! Now, what was that French I learned in school? O&ugrave; est ma chatte?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mouse<br /></strong>Chatte? Cat! Did you say cat?!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh, I'm so sorry Mouse! I forgot mice don't like cats.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mouse<br /></strong>Would you like cats if you were me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Well… perhaps not. But my cat Dinah is different. She's such a sweet, quiet thing.&nbsp;<strong>If you meet her, I'm sure you'll like her.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Mouse<br /></strong>We won't talk about cats any more, thank you!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>We won't! Er… do you - do you er… like dogs? They can be so sweet and they kill all the rats… and… Oh dear!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh please come back, dear Mouse.&nbsp;<strong>We won't talk about cats or dogs, if you don't like them</strong>. Swim with me to the shore.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>So Alice and the mouse swam to the edge of the pool of tears. And as they swam, they were joined by lots of other&nbsp;<strong>creatures</strong>&nbsp;that had fallen into the pool, just like Alice and the mouse. There was a duck and a&nbsp;<strong>dodo&nbsp;</strong>and many other strange animals that Alice had never seen before. All the creatures had the same question.</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>How can we get dry? What can we do? I'm so far away from my nest, that pool was very wet and salty, oh it's no good for my fur, etc…</p> 
 <p><strong>Dodo<br /></strong>We must have a Caucus-race!</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>Hooray! Hoorah!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>What's a Caucus-race, Mr Dodo?</p> 
 <p><strong>Dodo<br /></strong>The best way to explain a Caucus-race is to have a Caucus-race!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>It was the strangest race Alice had ever seen. The Dodo marked a circle for the racecourse and everyone stood anywhere they wanted to. Nobody said &quot;One, two, three, go!&quot; but everyone started running. Alice ran too, although she didn't quite know where she should run to. Everyone ran left and right in any direction they pleased. But after half an hour of running, everybody was quite dry again.</p> 
 <p><strong>Dodo<br /></strong>The race is over!</p> 
 <p><strong>Multiple voices<br /></strong>But who has won? Did I win? Who is the winner?</p> 
 <p><strong>Dodo<br /></strong>Ah... yes... Who has won? Who has won? Everybody has won and everyone must have&nbsp;<strong>prizes</strong>! And she must give the prizes!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice didn't have any prizes for a Caucus-race with her, but she searched in her pockets and found some sweets. She had enough sweets to give exactly one sweet to every runner. &nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Here you are, one for you, and one for you…</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>Thank you very much… oh dear, this has no taste whatsoever… oh, I shall choke…it's rather good, yes very tasty…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>And one for you – now, does everybody have one? Oh, I must say, my cat Dinah would love a Caucus-race…</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>Let's go! Come away! Time for bed! Oh, is it that time already? Cats - ugh!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh dear. I said it again. Come back! Please! I'm sorry! Poor Dinah. Nobody seems to like her down here and I'm sure she's the best cat in the world!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Poor Alice felt very lonely and sad. She cried quietly to herself for a while. But in a little while, she heard footsteps in the distance. She looked up to see who it was. Next time, I'll tell you who the footsteps belonged to, and how Alice got so big she filled a whole house, and what happened when she kicked poor Bill the lizard up and out of the chimney. Goodbye.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello! Alice is having some very&nbsp;<strong>curious</strong>&nbsp;adventures at the bottom of a rabbit hole. She drank a drink that made her very small indeed. But she wants to grow bigger so that she can reach the key that will unlock the tiny door to a beautiful garden. After eating some cake she found in a little glass box, Alice started to feel something …</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Curiouser and curiouser! I'm growing! My feet are so far away. Goodbye feet! How will I put my shoes and socks on, I wonder? Ouch!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice grew so big that her head hit the&nbsp;<strong>ceiling</strong>! It was easy to reach the table now. She picked up the tiny key and rushed to the door. But in her excitement, she forgot something again…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ohhhh… this is hopeless! I'm much too big for this door now! I'll never get into the garden! I can only look through the door with one eye! Oh…</p>

 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The sight of The White Rabbit,&nbsp;<strong>splendidly</strong>&nbsp;dressed in his best clothes, and carrying a large&nbsp;<strong>fan</strong>&nbsp;and a pair of white leather gloves was enough to stop Alice's tears.</p>

 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Oh!! Oh my!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Don't go! I won't hurt – Oh dear! You've dropped your gloves… But look: what a pretty fan. And crying is such hot work. Oh, that's better. Oh dear… how strange everything is today. Yesterday things were normal. But today I'm not sure if I am the same girl who woke up this morning. But, if I'm not the girl who woke up this morning, the question is, &quot;Who am I?&quot;</p>

 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh: Here's that feeling again.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Then something kept happening. Alice kept fanning herself.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I don't believe it. I must be… I am! I'm growing smaller again. Smaller than the table. Hello feet! It's good to see you again.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Soon Alice was smaller than ever. She was still&nbsp;<strong>shrinking</strong>&nbsp;and shrinking and she didn't know why.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh dear - I'm getting very small. Oh… I'm getting much too small! Oh dear - I shall fade away altogether! Ohh…! The fan? The fan!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Just in time. Alice threw the fan on the floor, so she wouldn't get any smaller. &nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>That was a lucky<strong>&nbsp;escape</strong>! But now I'm small enough to get into the garden!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Poor Alice! There she stood at the little door - but it was locked again. And there was the little key, back in its place, out of reach, on the table.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh not again! This is hopeless. I'll never get that key now. I so badly wanted to see the garden. And things are worse than ever - I've never been so small as this in my life. Never!</p>

 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ohhh!</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. This is the story of an ordinary girl called Alice. Our story begins on an ordinary summer's day. Let's meet Alice: here she is, sitting next to the river with her sister on a very hot summer's afternoon. Her sister is reading a book, and with no-one to talk to, Alice is bored… and a bit sleepy. Soon, she'll be in a Wonderland full of strange and wonderful adventures… but Alice doesn't know that yet…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ohh… There's nothing to do… except lie on the grass and pick&nbsp;<strong>daisies.&nbsp;</strong>Shall I make a daisy chain for my dear little Dinah? Oh… I don't know… it's sooo hot… &nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Oh dear! Oh dear! I'm late! I'm so very late! Oh dear oh dear!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>A white rabbit! A talking white rabbit? Perhaps. But a rabbit with a pocket-watch? A rabbit with pockets? I must see where he's going!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice had never seen a rabbit with a pocket, or a waistcoat, or a pocket-watch before. So, she ran after the rabbit as fast as she could, and when the rabbit jumped down a large rabbit hole, Alice jumped straight after him.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oohhhh… Either this hole is very deep or I'm falling very slowly. And what a curious rabbit-hole! Who would think a rabbit-hole would have bookshelves … and books … and maps … and jars of&nbsp;<strong>marmalade</strong>?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice fell down, down, down. She fell for so long that she began to think about Dinah, her cat.</p>

 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ouch! Who's there?</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Oh, my ears and whiskers! How late it's getting!!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Wait! Please sir, wait a moment!</p>

Alice tried to open the doors – but they were all locked. Then she saw a table with a tiny key on it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>These doors are all too big. There must be a smaller door somewhere. I wonder… hmmm, let me look behind this little curtain… ooh! a tiny little door! Let me try the key… What a beautiful garden! But how can I visit it? The door is so tiny – I can't even fit my head through! Oh! It's no use. I wish I could fold up like a&nbsp;<strong>telescope!</strong> Wait a minute… what's this? It certainly wasn't here before. A bottle –&nbsp;<strong>I wonder what it is?</strong>&nbsp;Let me see the label. Hmmm: Drink me… Oh! Oh! Ohhhhhh!!!! What a curious feeling! I'm folding up like a telescope!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And so she was! Alice got smaller and smaller until she was small enough to fit through the door. But she'd forgotten something …</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>The key!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice was too small to reach the key on the table. She tried and tried to climb up the table leg but it was too slippery. When she had tired herself out with trying, poor little Alice sat down and cried.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>It's no use. I can't reach the key, so I can't get into the garden and that's that. There's no use crying like that! Alice! I advise you to stop this minute! Oohh… what's this? A little glass box… with cake inside! Ooh: and there's a note. Eat me. Hmmm.&nbsp;<strong>I wonder if it will make me grow...</strong>&nbsp;if I grow, I will be able to reach the key. But what if makes me even smaller? Well, if it makes me smaller, I will be able to&nbsp;<strong>creep</strong>&nbsp;under the door.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And Alice began to eat the cake. Did she grow big enough to reach the key? Or perhaps the cake made her small enough to creep under the door and into her beautiful garden. I'll tell you what happened next time. Goodbye.&nbsp;</p>

"<p><strong>TODAY - IN THE ARCTIC</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Hello I'm Captain Walton. Something unexpected happened on my way here to the Arctic. I still can't make sense of it. I and my crew found this poor man on the ice. He was half dead when we rescued him. He said his name was Viktor Frankenstein. He was a good man but a very sad one. He told us a very strange story about a monster he created. And this monster was responsible for many deaths. He said he wished to warn me about the dangers of science but I think what he wanted was to get that story off of his chest. We took care of him but unfortunately he died. Poor man. What a crazy story!</p> 
 <p><strong>Crewman<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Captain, I have some good news.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Yes, sailor.</p> 
 <p><strong>Crewman<br clear=""none"" /></strong>There's a change in the wind. It's warmer. The ice <strong>is disappearing</strong> and we <strong>are going to be</strong> able to continue our trip to the North Pole.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>That is really good news. Thank you.</p> 
 <p><strong>Crewman<br clear=""none"" /></strong>I <strong>thought</strong> you needed some cheering up. It's sad what <strong>happened</strong> to that poor man, Frankenstein, who died earlier, isn't it? We gave him blankets, hot soup, but he was already very weak.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Yes. Yes, I know. What else could we have done?</p> 
 <p><strong>Crewman<br clear=""none"" /></strong><strong>Do you think</strong> that story he told us is true? About the monster? I remember the big shadow we saw far away, in the middle of the ice, before we rescued Frankenstein.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Yes, it was moving very quickly before it disappeared. But maybe it was something else. How can we be sure? All <strong>we've been able to see</strong> for weeks is this ice!</p> 
 <p><strong>Crewman<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Yes. I guess so. Well sir, let me go back to preparing the ship to continue our journey.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>What's... what's that? Someone's crying. The sound is coming from the cabin where Frankenstein's body is. Let me see what this is...</p> 
 <p><strong>IN THE SHIP'S CABIN</strong>&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Oh, who... who're you? You're so big, and...</p> 
 <p><strong>Creature<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Ugly. You mean ugly.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>You must be the Creature! His story was true!</p> 
 <p><strong>Creature<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Yes. He built me and brought me to life... to a very sad life. Now <strong>he's gone</strong>. I found him dead.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Well, at least... at least he's in peace now. He was carrying great pain in his heart. But <strong>why are you holding</strong> his body and crying? I thought you wanted to kill him?</p> 
 <p><strong>Creature<br clear=""none"" /></strong>I came to tell him I'm so very sorry.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Sorry?! Is it true? Maybe you're crying because you can't hurt him anymore. You caused him so many problems! All those deaths...</p> 
 <p><strong>Creature<br clear=""none"" /></strong>And what good has it done? I wanted to be kind and have love and friendship. But all I got was hatred. People feared me, they attacked me. And I hated them and attacked them in return. Now I hate myself.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>And so <strong>what are you going to do</strong>?<strong> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Creature<br clear=""none"" /></strong>Only death can end my suffering. I'll go north, build a fire and throw myself into the flames. Then it will be over.</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>But are... are you sure? Does it have to be this way?</p> 
 <p><strong>Creature<br clear=""none"" /></strong>That's the only way. My body will be blown to the sea by the wind and my spirit will finally be free. Goodbye, Frankenstein. Goodbye, sir. Don't follow me.&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Captain<br clear=""none"" /></strong>There goes the Creature running fast across the ice. What a powerful being and how sorry he was! Oh, <strong>he's disappeared</strong> now... Poor creature. In the future we might know him as Frankenstein. That was the name of his creator. He, or... it, didn't even get a name. It's just called the Creature. A Creature which will never be seen again.</p>

"<p><strong><span>TODAY – IN THE ARCTIC</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>Hello, I'm scientist Viktor Frankenstein. And I'm here in the Arctic, the end of the Earth, because I'm looking for the Creature which destroyed my happiness. The last time I was happy was… with Elizabeth. Our wedding day was coming…</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>IN THE PAST – AT THE FRANKENSTEIN'S HOME IN GENEVA</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Elizabeth<br /></span></strong><span>Let me check the guest list again</span><span>…</span><span> How many guests</span><span> have we planned earlier, Mr Frankenstein?</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein's Father<br /></span></strong><span>There were 60, the last time I counted, dear Elizabeth. </span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Elizabeth<br /></span></strong><span>Is the house<strong> big enough </strong></span><span>for all our guests?</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein's Father<br /></span></strong><span>Yes, it is, my darling. Invite more people. Let's have a banquet and plenty of good wine! </span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Elizabeth<br /></span></strong><span>How much wine</span><span> shall we order? Are two hundred bottles <strong>too many</strong></span><span>?</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein's Father<br /></span></strong><span>No.</span><span>I'll pay for it all gladly. Nothing is </span><strong><span>too expensive</span></strong><span> for my dear son and his bride. Let's all drink and b</span><span>e merry! It will be a wedding nobody will ever forget! Are you happy, my dear?</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Elizabeth<br /></span></strong><span>Oh, I'm <strong>very </strong></span><span>happy! </span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>TODAY – IN THE ARCTIC</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>It's <strong>very</strong></span><span> cold here! Well, Elizabeth and I got married on a warm day. There was a lot of catching up with friends. Elizabeth looked so pretty. But I was worried. I got used to walking around with a gun in my pocket. The threat by the Creature was </span><strong><span>very</span></strong><span> much alive in my mind…</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>IN THE PAST</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Creature<br /></span></strong><span>I'll have my revenge. I'll be with you on your wedding night!</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>TODAY – IN THE ARCTIC</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>I didn't give the monster a bride so it said it would destroy my life. It killed my best friend Henry, my brother William and his nanny Justine was blamed for the boy's murder… and now it was coming after me. This was in my thoughts when we arrived for our honeymoon at the house we rented by the side of Lake Como in Italy. It was raining heavily…</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>IN THE PAST – AT A HOUSE BY LAKE COMO, ITALY</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Elizabeth<br /></span></strong><span>It's a pity we have to close the windows. The view of the lake is fantastic!</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>Yes. But I'm sure the rain won't last. Why don't you go to the bedroom, my darling? </span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Elizabeth<br /></span></strong><span>Aren't you coming?</span><span>What are you looking for, dear Viktor? </span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>I just want to make sure that everything is alright and we are safe. I'll go as soon as I do that, my sweet Elizabeth. </span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Elizabeth<br /></span></strong><span>Are you expecting someone?</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>No, darling wife. Go and I'll join you as soon as I can. I don't want anything to worry you.</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>TODAY – IN THE ARCTIC</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>I was indeed expecting something to happen: a battle to the death between me and the Creature. I didn't care if it was too strong for me. I had <strong>enough</strong></span><span> hate in my heart to defeat the monster. I just didn't want Elizabeth to see the fight. I left the house with my gun and decided to walk around to check if it was there. But all of a sudden, a scream…</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>IN THE PAST – AT A HOUSE BY LAKE COMO, ITALY</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Elizabeth<br /></span></strong><span>Ahhhhhhh!</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>Elizabeth! Elizabeth!</span></p> 
 <p><strong>INSIDE THE HOUSE</strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>My dear Elizabeth! My beloved wife… is dead!!</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Creature<br /></span></strong><span>Ah! Ah! Ah! Ah!</span><span><br /></span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>You, horrible Creature! I'll kill you! I'll put a bullet in your head!</span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>SHOOTING</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>I hate you! I hate you with all my heart! My Elizabeth! </span></p> 
 <p><strong><span>TODAY – IN THE ARCTIC</span></strong></p> 
 <p><strong><span>Viktor Frankenstein<br /></span></strong><span>William, Justine, Henry and now Elizabeth. There was nothing else for me and… for my father. As soon as he heard that my wife was killed on our wedding night, he fell ill and died heartbroken. And all because of me! I'd thought about telling Elizabeth that I had created a monster. But there wasn't <strong>enough</strong></span><span> time… After her death I tried to warn others and I was put in a hospital for a while. Nobody believed me… So I decided to put an end to the problem I had created and find the creature at once. The world </span><strong><span>is not big enough</span></strong><span> for both of us. I'm still looking for it. I might find it next time.</span></p>
