"<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I now know that my uncle is involved in smuggling. I also&nbsp;<strong>suspect</strong>&nbsp;that he has murdered a man. But if I tell, my aunt will suffer, so I can't do anything. Today, I am alone cleaning the kitchen. But the quiet does not last...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary</strong><br />Who can that be?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator</strong><br />When I go in the bar, there's a man with a glass of beer. He looks familiar…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>What do you think you're doing? You can't help yourself to drink!</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Are you the barmaid?&nbsp;<strong>Fill up</strong>&nbsp;my glass.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong><strong>Fill it up</strong>&nbsp;yourself. I'll tell Mr Merlyn you are here.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Don't&nbsp;<strong>bother -&nbsp;</strong>he won't want to see me…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Well, I can't stand here waiting.&nbsp;<strong>Pay up</strong>&nbsp;and you can go.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Do you order Joss around like that?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>He's my uncle. Patience was my mother's sister. Now, I have work to do… uncle!</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Who the hell are you talking to? I told you to keep your mouth shut! Oh, it's you, Jem. What do you want? You can&nbsp;<strong>get on with</strong>&nbsp;your work, Mary…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>So that was Jem, my uncle's brother. He's got the same dark eyes and hair, but drink has not ruined his face – it's younger and more handsome.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Excuse me -&nbsp;I didn't expect to see a girl like you at Jamaica Inn.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>My mother died, so I came here. I'm glad she isn't alive to see how my aunt lives now. I&nbsp;try to help her in the house. What do you do?</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>I steal horses.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oh! Aren't you afraid of being caught?</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Not really. Listen, I'm being serious now. Jamaica Inn is no place for you with its ugly business. I can help you go to Bodmin.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I don't need help. I can&nbsp;<strong>look after</strong>&nbsp;myself.</p> 
 <p><strong>Jem<br /></strong>Well... I'm going now. But remember – I live in Trewartha if you ever need me.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>How can I trust him? He's a thief -&nbsp;and he's Joss's brother. The loneliness of my situation grips me again.</p> 
 <p>The men have returned. From my window, I can see them lifting heavy objects onto the wagons. These men are&nbsp;<strong>desperate</strong>&nbsp;and dangerous. And Jem…? Did he come to warn his brother that they were coming?</p> 
 <p>This morning, I'm doing the washing. My uncle is away, so I can almost feel the happiness I used to feel when I worked on the farm.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>What is it?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mr Bassat is here - &nbsp;the&nbsp;<strong>magistrate,&nbsp;</strong>with another man. What are we going to do? He's never been before: he must know something.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>What am I going to say?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>This is my chance to tell an officer about Joss - but look at my aunt. She is trembling and terrified.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Just say Joss is away.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary, you won't tell Mr Bassat about the wagons, will you? If anything happens to Joss, I'll kill myself.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>You took your time. Where's the landlord?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>He's not here. &nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>When will he be back?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>He went out after breakfast. I don't know when he's&nbsp;<strong>getting back.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong><strong>Damn!&nbsp;</strong>Listen to me – your husband is giving this whole area - my land - a bad&nbsp;<strong>reputation</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>I don't know what you mean. We live a quiet life here&nbsp;- my niece will tell you!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>I'm not a fool. We'll look around now we are here.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>Mr Bassat is having a good look around the inn. He knows there is something hidden here.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>This place is a&nbsp;<strong>disgrace</strong>! Call yourself an inn! There isn't one clean room.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary, Mary -&nbsp;the room by the bar!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>We come to the locked room.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I'm afraid this room is locked.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>Why?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I don't know…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>Have you ever heard wheels and horses at night?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>No, never.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>Where is the key to the room?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>My uncle has it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mr Bassat<br /></strong>Well, we'll have to&nbsp;<strong>break down</strong>&nbsp;the door, then.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I'm afraid. I hate lying to save my uncle -&nbsp;and part of me will be glad if they find&nbsp;<strong>evidence&nbsp;</strong>of his crimes. I remember the rope. But the fear of what might lie behind the door is clear in my aunt's eyes. For her, it would be the end.</p> 
 <p>In the next episode – I meet a man who I can talk to and tell him about the awful things I have seen – but can he be trusted?</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I've not seen my uncle much since I arrived. I am glad because he's got a violent temper and treats my aunt badly. This morning, I've been exploring the country around the inn…</p> 
 <p>There is nothing but&nbsp;<strong>heather&nbsp;</strong>and grass for miles. In the distance I can see the&nbsp;<strong>marsh.&nbsp;</strong>It was in this wild and lonely land that my uncle lived as a boy with his two brothers. Last night he told me their story.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>If you had lived here, you would have taken to drink, like I did… it makes you do things. I had a family once: a father, mother, two brothers, but&nbsp;<strong>each one of them</strong>&nbsp;disappeared one way or another. My father was&nbsp;<strong>hanged</strong>. He killed a man. My brother Jem is clever – but they'll catch him, too and hang him. My brother Matthew – well, he drowned in the marsh. They found him one summer when the marsh dried up…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator</strong><br />When I get back to the inn my uncle is there...</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Well, did you miss me?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Did you have a nice trip?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Nice,&nbsp;<strong>be</strong>&nbsp;<strong>damned</strong>. I've been riding for four days. There was a bit of money involved - that's all I care about.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Well, I'll go and help my aunt...</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>It's me you'll be helping tonight, in the bar...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>It's Saturday night – the bar is crowded. The air is full of smoke and the smell of unwashed bodies.&nbsp;<strong>All of them</strong>&nbsp;are drunk. Some men are so drunk that they lie on the benches like dead men.</p> 
 <p><strong>Harry (man in bar)<br /></strong>Another pint…</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Hurry up there, girl.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Uncle, I cannot&nbsp;<strong>bear</strong>&nbsp;this. I'm going upstairs.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Too good for us are you? Well it's almost midnight now. Go to your room and lock your door …</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oww! Let go of my wrist! You're hurting me!</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Hear this: Keep your mouth shut, and you won't get hurt - but if you start to ask...</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Oh! What's that noise? It's coming from under my room…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>The moonlight pours into my room creating ghostly shadows. I creep over to the window. My uncle is below and I recognise other men from earlier this evening. There are four or five&nbsp;<strong>wagons.</strong>&nbsp;The men have been taking big boxes from them into the inn.</p> 
 <p><strong>Harry<br /></strong>That's the last of them.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Good. Get going now. Be quick…</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>What will you do about him?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Don't worry. Harry and I will deal with him later…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I understand now. They are&nbsp;<strong>smuggling!</strong>&nbsp;Jamaica Inn is a perfect place for it. But what's my uncle doing at the moment? I have to go and see…</p> 
 <p>As I get closer to the bar, I hear voices. I hide in the shadows.</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>No, and no again – I will not be a part of it - that's murder you are talking about Mr Merlyn … killing&nbsp;<strong>innocent</strong>&nbsp;women and children – no!</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Not so fast! By God, you will do as I say. Another man said the same and he was hanging at the end of a rope a few minutes later! Harry – you go and lock the door behind you. I'll finish here…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I feel sick. My heart has been beating so loudly, I am sure they have heard it. I go back to my room quietly…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>What shall I do? If I had a gun or a knife, I could perhaps hurt my uncle so that the man can escape…But I have nothing …I must do something, though ….</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I creep downstairs again. The door to the bar is shut. There is silence. I suddenly know I have to open the door to find out.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>There's no one here! Just the tables and a few empty glasses…The door is open at the back. But wait… what's that hanging in the middle of the room? It's swinging… A rope hanging from a hook in the ceiling! But there's nothing on the end of it. What's happened to that man? I fear the worst…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator</strong><br />Next time we meet, an interesting visitor arrives at Jamaica Inn. But who is he and can he be trusted?</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>I have arrived at Jamaica Inn to live with my aunt. My uncle is landlord here. It's a cold and lonely place. I'm at the door and I'm waiting for someone to let me in…</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Who's there?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>It's me. Mary. Mary Yellan.</p> 
 <p>[Heavy door opening]</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Ah, so, you've arrived at last. Well, say hello to your Uncle Joss.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Where is my Aunt Patience?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>What's the hurry? Don't you want to give me a big kiss first? Patience! She's here. [impatiently] Where are you, woman?</p> 
 <p>Patience! Where in hell is that woman?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>I'm here. Is it the girl?</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>See for yourself.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>A woman with grey hair hurries towards me. In the candlelight her face is pale. She looks afraid.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Aunt Patience - I am so glad to see you.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>But she is unrecognisable. Her curls have gone and her happy smile also. I can see that&nbsp;<strong>she's been crying</strong>. This woman is old and anxious. She starts to cry.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Stop&nbsp;<strong>whimpering</strong>, woman. Can't you see the girl is hungry! I'll take her things up to her room. If there's nothing to eat on the table when I come down, you'll soon have something to cry about.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>He lifts my heavy box as if it's a bag of feathers. He is huge with shoulders like those of a bear.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>The kitchen is full of smoke from the fire. There are&nbsp;<strong>stains</strong>&nbsp;on the stone floor and there's a strong smell of alcohol. On the table there are two empty bottles of&nbsp;<strong>brandy</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>You mustn't mind your Uncle Joss. Some people find him strange at first, but he is very&nbsp;<strong>respected</strong>&nbsp;here. Just yesterday he told me that a man stopped and told him how much he admired.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Are you talking rubbish again woman? Sit down Mary. Eat. Listen, Mary. I'm in charge here and you'll do as I say. You'll serve the customers in the bar and help in the house. But if you open your mouth and&nbsp;<strong>squawk</strong>&nbsp;like a hen, you'll be sorry.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I'll help you like you say, but if you hurt my aunt, I'll tell and you'll be&nbsp;<strong>punished</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Patience, go and get me another bottle and be quick. Big words – maybe we're not so different, Mary. Here, drink this.This is my&nbsp;<strong>curse</strong>, Mary – drink.&nbsp;<strong>I've been drinking a little today but</strong>&nbsp;- Oh you'll see how we drink here some Saturdays – they hear the shouting and singing far away. People are afraid of me but I'm afraid of no one. Go to bed now.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>He suddenly grabs my wrist.</p> 
 <p><strong>Joss<br /></strong>Listen carefully. Some nights you'll hear wheels, footsteps and voices outside. You must stay in your room and put your blanket over your ears. If you ask questions, I'll break every bone in your body. Do you understand?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>My room is small and&nbsp;<strong>bare.&nbsp;</strong>Just a bed and a table with a broken mirror. I feel lonely and&nbsp;<strong>trapped&nbsp;</strong>like a bird in a cage. But it's not too late to run away. I&nbsp;<strong>creep</strong>&nbsp;down the dark passage.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>[to herself] Who's crying? It must be my aunt!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>I turn back. My uncle frightens me but I must stay and protect Aunt Patience.</p> 
 <p>I did not sleep well last night. My bed is hard and the blanket is thin. The house is quiet this morning. I'll look for a place to wash downstairs. Here is the bar. Ah, there's a passage here – maybe it's along here. A&nbsp;door – this must be the washroom.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>How strange – it's locked.</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary! What are you doing?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Why is this room locked, Aunt Patience? What's in it?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>My aunt looks quickly behind her and her eyes are like a frightened rabbit's.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Is it because of the people who come to the inn at night?</p> 
 <p><strong>Patience<br /></strong>Mary. Mary.<strong>&nbsp;I've been worrying about how to tell you this</strong>. I must warn you. Bad things happen here. Men come at night and they go into that room with Joss. When you hear them, you must stay in your room. You must never ask me or your uncle about it again.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrating<br /></strong>What is in this room and why is my Aunt so scared? I'm not going to like it here but I must stay to support her and keep her safe. Next time we meet – I have to work in the bar of Jamaica Inn on Saturday night where I get to meet a group of rough and drunk men. Later that night there are some strange goings-on in the yard outside.&nbsp; What's going on at Jamaica Inn?</p>

"<p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>My name is Mary, Mary Yellan. I'm 23 years old.&nbsp;<strong>I'm not usually very brave, but I feel brave today.</strong>&nbsp;Here I am… on this long journey to Cornwall… on my own.&nbsp;<strong>I've left the farm</strong>&nbsp;where&nbsp;<strong>I've lived all my life</strong>. I wanted to stay there, but last week I made a promise to my dear Mother…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>[coughing/weak voice] Mary, my child… listen… I won't be in this world much longer.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Don't say that, Mother.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>It's true, Mary. But, before I go,&nbsp;<strong>I have only one wish</strong>…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Yes, Mother dear?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>When I die, promise me you will go and live with my sister, Patience.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>But why can't I stay here on the farm, here in Helford?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>You can't stay here alone.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>But&nbsp;<strong>I haven't seen Patience since I was a child</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mother<br /></strong>I know, but soon she will be the only family you have. [coughing]&nbsp;<strong>I have written to her. She has agreed</strong>&nbsp;that you can go and live with her and your uncle Joshua.&nbsp;<strong>They live on Bodmin Moor in Cornwall</strong>. Here, take her letter.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Bodmin Moor! But that's so far away!</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>Mother died last Tuesday. The funeral was yesterday. We buried her next to Papa.&nbsp;<strong>Now, I'm on my way to my aunt's house.&nbsp; I've got the letter here</strong>…</p> 
 <p>[reading]<strong>&nbsp;Joss and I now live in Jamaica Inn</strong>, where he is&nbsp;<strong>landlord</strong>. It's on the road between Bodmin and Launceston…</p> 
 <p>This journey is so long! We have been travelling for hours. What a wild and lonely county Cornwall is. My only&nbsp;<strong>consolation&nbsp;</strong>is that I will see my aunt again after so many years. Oh how pretty she was with her golden hair and blue eyes! Always laughing, enjoying ourselves…</p> 
 <p>But&nbsp;<strong>I never visited her&nbsp;</strong>and I never met her husband either. … Ah, at last, I can see houses and people – this must be Bodmin town.</p> 
 <p>There is just me and one other traveller left. It's so cold and grey outside…&nbsp;<strong>The rain is lashing against the window</strong>. I wish it would stop! All I can see is mile upon mile of empty&nbsp;<strong>moorland</strong>. No trees… no houses… I wonder how many more hours we have to travel?</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Excuse me, sir – is it much further?</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong><strong>Where are you going?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>Jamaica Inn…&nbsp;<strong>Do you know it?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>Maybe I do and maybe I don't… and&nbsp;<strong>why are you going there?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I'm going to live there… with my aunt and uncle.</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>That will be Joss Merlyn...&nbsp;<strong>People say that queer things go on at Jamaica Inn</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong><strong>What do you mean – queer?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>It's just what they say. But&nbsp;<strong>respectable people don't go there any more</strong>. It's a lonely place.</p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>If I were you, Miss,&nbsp; I would go on to Launceston tonight and go back to Bodmin tomorrow.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>But I can't.<strong>&nbsp;My aunt and uncle are waiting for me.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Man<br /></strong>Jamaica Inn is no place for a young woman.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>I have nowhere else to go…</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>What can he mean by 'queer things'?&nbsp;<strong>Why is he looking at me in that curious way?</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Driver<br /></strong>Whoa boy…! Slow now.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong><strong>Why have we stopped here</strong>&nbsp;– it's the middle of nowhere?</p> 
 <p><strong>Driver<br /></strong>Jamaica Inn! There you go Miss.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary<br /></strong>But there's nothing here! Oh – what's that? There up on the&nbsp;<strong>moor</strong>&nbsp;- a dark building with tall chimneys. I can see a path to the door. There's a sign twisting in the wind. It says 'Jamaica Inn'.</p> 
 <p><strong>Mary narrator<br /></strong>Suddenly&nbsp;<strong>I feel frightened. I want to climb back in the coach.</strong></p> 
 <p>Too late –&nbsp;<strong>it's already gone</strong>... I suppose my only choice now is to enter Jamaica Inn.</p> 
 <p>Next time we meet – I get to meet my Aunt Patience and Uncle Joss. I discover what a mean and scary man my uncle is. And I discover a locked room – what is inside? &nbsp;&nbsp;</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. Alice has had lots of adventures in Wonderland. Now, she has been called as a witness in the trial of the Knave of Hearts. The King of Hearts is the judge, but Alice has grown so tall that her head reaches the top of the courthouse and all the people seem very far away.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>How small you all are!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>The witness must come to the witness box!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice jumped up and knocked over the jury box. It was full of animals and they all fell out.</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>Ooh, ow, oh are you hurt? Excuse me, is that my chair? Etc...</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'm so sorry!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>What do you know about this business?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Nothing at all!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The King looked in his Book of&nbsp;<strong>Rules</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Rule forty-two. &quot;All&nbsp;<strong>persons</strong>&nbsp;more than a mile high must leave the court.&quot;</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'm not a mile high!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Indeed you are not! You are nearly two miles high!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Well, I'm not going! And&nbsp;<strong>you can't make</strong>&nbsp;me!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice had grown a little bit more, and the King, who was now the size of Alice's shoe,&nbsp;<strong>could see</strong>&nbsp;she was right about that part. His face went very&nbsp;<strong>pale</strong>&nbsp;and he closed&nbsp;his Book of Rules.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>White Rabbit. Ask the jury: what is their decision about this matter? Did the Knave steal the Queen's tarts?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>But there was more&nbsp;<strong>evidence.</strong>&nbsp;The White Rabbit gave a letter to the King, who opened it and turned to the Knave of Hearts.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Knave of Hearts, did you write this?</p> 
 <p><strong>Knave of Hearts<br /></strong>I didn't write it! Look at the end of it: there is no name written there!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Then you are not a honest man! An honest man always signs his work! Read the letter!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And the White Rabbit read the letter. No-one understood a single word of it.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>That's the most important evidence we've heard today!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I don't believe there's any meaning in it!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>If there's no meaning in it, then we don't need to try to find any! Jury, what is your decision?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The Queen stamped her feet.</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>No, no no!&nbsp;<strong>Punishment</strong>&nbsp;first, decision afterwards!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>That's nonsense! The punishment comes last!</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Be quiet!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I won't!</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Off with her head!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>No-one moved. Alice realised she had grown to her full size.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Who cares about you? All of you!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice looked down at the little people all around her. She suddenly realised…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>You're nothing but a pack of cards!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>As soon as she said this, the animals, the birds, the King and Queen and everyone else turned into a pack of cards and they all flew up into the air and came flying down upon her. The cards fluttered and flew all around her head and shoulders and Alice gave a scream as she tried to beat them off with her hands…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ohhhh!!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And then another strange thing happened to Alice. She found herself back on the riverbank where our story began. She opened her eyes and saw her sister smiling at her.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice's sister<br /></strong>Wake up, Alice dear! What a long sleep you've had!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice's sister gently brushed away some dead leaves that had fallen from the tree and onto her face.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh… I've had such a curious dream.&nbsp;There was a White Rabbit and … I got bigger and smaller … and I met a caterpillar and a Hatter … and played croquet and … a cat that smiled and … so many things.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice told her sister all about the Wonderland in her dream and the adventures she had had there. Perhaps one day Alice will dream herself back to Wonderland. If she does, I'll be sure to tell you. Goodbye.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. Alice is having lots adventures in Wonderland. Now, she's in a courtroom full of animals. Everybody is waiting for the trial to start. The Queen and King of Hearts have already arrived and they are sitting on their&nbsp;<strong>thrones</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>May I sit here? Please do. Who is on trial? What is the crime? Oh dear, I can't find my glasses. Where is the prisoner? Is it that girl? No, I don't think so…</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The rest of the room was filled with birds and animals and the whole pack of playing-card people. Alice saw the White Rabbit. He was holding a&nbsp;<strong>trumpet&nbsp;</strong>in one hand and a large piece of paper in the other. The White Rabbit blew the trumpet.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Silence in court!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The trial started. The King was the judge and twelve animals were the jury. The King spoke first.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Read the accusation!</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>The Queen of Hearts, she made some&nbsp;<strong>tarts</strong>,<br />All on a summer day.<br />The Knave of Hearts, he stole those tarts<br />And took them quite away.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Knave of Hearts, what do you say?</p> 
 <p><strong>Knave of Hearts<br /></strong>It wasn't me! I didn't do it!</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Silence! Call the first&nbsp;<strong>witness</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Bring in the first witness!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The first witness was the Hatter. He looked very&nbsp;<strong>nervous</strong>. He came into the court with a cup of tea in one shaking hand and a piece of bread and butter in the other.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Give your evidence Hatter, and don't be nervous, or you'll lose your head!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The King's words made the Hatter even more frightened. He was so confused and that he took a large bite out of his teacup instead of his bread and butter.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter<br /></strong>I'm a poor man, your Majesty.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>You're a very poor speaker.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Poor Hatter. He&nbsp;<strong>didn't use to be</strong>&nbsp;mad, you know. He&nbsp;<strong>used to be</strong>&nbsp;quite normal.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>And&nbsp;<strong>I used to be taller</strong>…</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Just then, Alice began to have a curious feeling.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ohh.. I'm growing again!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>No-one noticed that Alice was getting taller. Everyone was watching the Hatter, who was too frightened to speak.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>You may go. Call the next witness!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The next witness was the cook.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Cook, what are tarts made of?</p> 
 <p><strong>Cook<br /></strong>Pepper, mostly.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Everybody started sneezing. Nobody seemed to notice Alice growing taller and taller. By the time they stopped sneezing, the cook had disappeared.</p> 
 <p><strong>King<br /></strong>Never mind! Call the next witness!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice watched as the White Rabbit studied the piece of paper, looking for the name of the next witness. Imagine her surprise when he straightened up, took a deep breath and shouted the name of the next witness…</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Alice!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Everybody in the courtroom turned to look at Alice. Alice felt herself grow a little taller, as she took a deep breath, and stepped forward. Next time, I'll tell you what happened when Alice gives her evidence and the White Rabbit reads a letter from the Knave of Hearts. Curiouser and curiouser… Goodbye.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello! After all her adventures, Alice has finally found the beautiful garden she's been looking for all this time. It's full of beautiful white roses. Alice wandered through the flowers until she saw a gardener. He was doing something very strange...</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Why are you painting the roses red?</p> 
 <p><strong>Gardener<br /></strong>The Queen - she wants red roses and I put white roses in by mistake. If the Queen finds them, she'll cut my head off! Oh no! Here comes the Queen!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The gardener threw himself to the ground and lay with his face down. A line of&nbsp;<strong>soldiers</strong>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<strong>courtiers</strong>&nbsp;came marching into the rose garden. They didn't look like people at all. They looked exactly like playing cards: their bodies were square and flat with their heads at the top and their hands and feet in the four corners. First came a group of ten soldiers, who were decorated with black clubs, then came ten of the Queen's servants, who were covered in red diamonds. Then came all the princes and princesses, wearing red hearts. The&nbsp;<strong>Knave of Hearts</strong>&nbsp;was carrying a crown on a cushion, and last of all came the King and Queen of Hearts. When they got to Alice, everybody stopped. The Queen looked at Alice.</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Who is this?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'm Alice,&nbsp;<strong>Your Majesty.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Can you play croquet?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Yes!</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Come on then! Everyone get to your places!</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>I'm over here... Are you over there? This is place, no this is your place, are we ready?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Everyone began running in different directions until they got into place and the game began. It was a very curious game: everything seemed to be alive! The balls were&nbsp;<strong>hedgehogs</strong>&nbsp;and the croquet mallets were&nbsp;<strong>flamingos</strong>. All the playing-card-soldiers bent over so they looked like&nbsp;<strong>arches</strong>. The players had to catch the flamingos first, which wasn't easy because they kept flying away. When the flamingos were caught, each player held their flamingo tightly under one arm, with the long neck and head hanging down to the ground. Then the hedgehogs curled up into spiky balls – and the players used the flamingos' heads to hit the hedgehogs so that they rolled through the playing-card soldier arches.</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals<br /></strong>Is it my turn? Oh good shot! Have another go... oh do stand still! Very nicely played, it's your turn again, very good, etc...</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>What a curious game! I suppose I should play.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>It was a very curious game! There didn't seem to be any rules. Everyone played at the same time and the hedgehogs kept running away. Alice took a flamingo and tried to hit a hedgehog with it. But the flamingo moved its head and she missed. Soon the players began arguing and fighting for the hedgehogs and the Queen went around stamping her feet and shouting at everyone.</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>Off with your head! Off with her head!</p> 
 <p><strong>Animals</strong><br />No it isn't your turn! That's my ball, give me my hedgehog! It's my turn, not yours! Is that my flamingo? That's cheating!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>How&nbsp;<strong>will I get out</strong>&nbsp;of here?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>As Alice was looking around for a way to escape, suddenly the Cheshire-Cat appeared in the air. He wasn't sitting on anything, he was just floating.</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>Are you enjoying the croquet?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>No. I don't think they play fairly at all. Everyone is arguing and there aren't any rules.</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>How do you like the Queen?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Not at all! I suppose I should try to play or&nbsp;<strong>she might cut off my head</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice went to find her hedgehog. She found it having a fight with another one. While she was trying to pull the two animals apart, her flamingo flew away.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh dear! I'm not doing very well at this game.&nbsp;<strong>What will the Queen think</strong>?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice was right to worry. Most of the other players had made the Queen angry for one reason or another and the soldiers took them away one by one. Soon there were only the King, the Queen and Alice left in the game. The Queen turned to Alice.</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>You! Come here! Who were you talking to?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>If you please, your Majesty...</p> 
 <p><strong>Voice<br /></strong>The&nbsp;<strong>trial&nbsp;</strong>is starting! The&nbsp;<strong>trial&nbsp;</strong>is starting!</p> 
 <p><strong>Queen<br /></strong>The trial! Oh good! I love trials! Come along!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice had no choice but to follow the Queen. We'll leave her there for now. Next time. I'll tell you all about the Knave of Hearts, the stolen jam tarts and what happened when Alice met the Hatter and The White Rabbit again. Goodbye.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Hello! Alice is trying to find her way back to the beautiful garden she saw when she first arrived in Wonderland.  <p><strong>March Hare</strong><br />You mean you know the answer, don't you?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />Yes, I do.</p> 
 <p><strong>March Hare</strong><br />Then you should say what you mean!</p>

 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />No. I give up. What's the answer?</p>

 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />I haven't had any tea, have I? So I can't take more.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter</strong><br />You mean you can't take less. It's very easy to take more than nothing.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Alice got up and walked off without saying goodbye.</p>

 <p><strong>Hatter</strong><br />Don't mind if I do!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />The Hatter and the March Hare didn't seem to notice her leaving. Alice went back into the woods. She looked back as she walked away. The Hatter and the March Hare were trying to put the mouse into the teapot.</p> 
 <p><strong>Hatter and Hare</strong><br />Mousey mousey! In you go! Plop! Oh, he does wriggle so. More tea?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />I'll never go there again! That was the stupidest tea-party I've ever been to in all my life!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Back in the woods, Alice saw a tree with a door in it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />That's very curious! I wonder what could be behind a door in a tree...</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />In Wonderland anything can be behind any door. Alice opened the door and there she was at the beginning of her adventures again – in the hall with the locked doors and the table with the little key on it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />I remember that little door and the key! This time I know what to do! I'm finally going to get into the garden!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Alice had learned a lot about growing and shrinking in Wonderland.  <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />Oh, it's so pretty here!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />We'll leave Alice here for now, happy in the garden at last. Soon, she's going to meet the Queen and play croquet. Will she still be happy then? I'll tell you next time.</p>

"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. Alice is in the woods. She's trying to find her way back to the beautiful garden that she saw when she first arrived in Wonderland. Here she is, outside a little house. She's wondering who lives there.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I wonder who could live in such a little house!</p>

 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>The Duchess!!</p>

 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And&nbsp;<strong>she found</strong>&nbsp;herself in a noisy, smoky kitchen.  <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>There's too much pepper in that soup! Please would you tell me why&nbsp;<strong>your cat grins</strong>&nbsp;like that?</p> 
 <p><strong>The Duchess<br /></strong>It's a Cheshire-Cat, and that's why.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong><strong>I didn't know</strong>&nbsp;Cheshire-Cats grinned. In fact<strong>, I didn't know</strong>&nbsp;cats could grin.</p> 
 <p><strong>The Duchess<br /></strong>You don't know much, and that's a fact.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Just then,&nbsp;<strong>the cook took</strong>&nbsp;the pan of soup off the fire, and&nbsp;<strong>started</strong>&nbsp;throwing&nbsp;<strong>pots and pans</strong>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<strong>plates and dishes</strong>&nbsp;all around the kitchen.&nbsp;<strong>Some of them hit</strong>&nbsp;the Duchess, but&nbsp;<strong>she didn't seem</strong>&nbsp;to notice.&nbsp;<strong>Some of them hit</strong>&nbsp;the baby, who was crying anyway.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh please! The baby! Be careful!</p> 
 <p><strong>The Duchess<br /></strong>Here! You hold it if you like!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And&nbsp;<strong>the Duchess threw</strong>&nbsp;the baby at Alice who just managed to catch it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ohhh!!</p> 
 <p><strong>The Duchess<br /></strong>I must go and get ready to play croquet with the Queen.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And, with that, The Duchess left.&nbsp;<strong>Alice held</strong>&nbsp;the baby and wondered what to do with it.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>What am I going to do with you? You're a strange shape… Oh! You're a not a baby. You're a… you're a pig!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>It was easy to decide what to do with a pig. Alice took it outside and let it go into the woods.&nbsp;<strong>The Cheshire-Cat sat</strong>&nbsp;in a tree and watched her.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Cheshire-Cat, could you tell me which way I should go?</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>A Hatter lives over here, and a March Hare lives over there. They're both&nbsp;<strong>mad</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>But I don't want to meet mad people.</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>Oh, we're all mad here. Are you playing croquet with the Queen today?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'd love to play croquet with the Queen… but&nbsp;<strong>she hasn't invited me</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Cheshire-Cat<br /></strong>You'll see me there…</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The cat disappeared. Alice set off in the direction of the March Hare's house and soon she came to a house. Outside the house she saw a tea-party quite unlike any tea-party she had ever seen before. Next time, I'll tell you all about the Tea Party and what happened when&nbsp;<strong>Alice met</strong>&nbsp;the March Hare and the Hatter. Goodbye.</p> 
 "
"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>After Alice frightened everyone by growing as big as a house, she ate some little cakes and&nbsp;<strong>shrank</strong>&nbsp;again. She&nbsp;<strong>doesn't like</strong>&nbsp;being so tiny, so she's looking for something to make her grow to the right size. But this is Wonderland and what she finds, sitting on top of a mushroom, is very curious indeed…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Am I as small as a mushroom, or is the mushroom as tall as me? Ohh!!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Sitting on top of the mushroom was a blue caterpillar smoking a&nbsp;<strong>hookah pipe.</strong></p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>Who are you?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I… I'm not sure.&nbsp;<strong>I know</strong>&nbsp;who I was when I woke up this morning. But I've changed so many times since then!</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>What do you mean by that? Explain yourself!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I can't explain myself because I'm not myself. It's very confusing…<strong>&nbsp;I think</strong>&nbsp;you should tell me who YOU are first.</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>Why?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ummm…</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice couldn't think of any good reason. She decided to leave.</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>Come back! I have something important to say!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Yes?&nbsp;</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>Don't be unhappy.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Is that all?</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>No. So you think you've changed, do you?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I have, sir. I don't stay the same size for more than ten minutes!</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>What size do you want to be?</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Oh,&nbsp;<strong>I don't mind</strong>. A little bit bigger is all I would like. Seven centimetres is such a terrible&nbsp;<strong>height</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>It is a very good height! I myself am exactly seven centimetres in height!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>And with that, the caterpillar crawled off the mushroom and away.</p> 
 <p><strong>Caterpillar<br /></strong>One side of the mushroom will make you grow taller. The other side will make you grow shorter. Seven centimetres indeed!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Hmmm… let me pull this side… and now this side…But which side is which?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>There was only one way to find out the answer to that question. Alice took a bite of one piece of the mushroom - and shrank so quickly that she hit her&nbsp;<strong>chin</strong>&nbsp;on her foot.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice</strong><br />Ouch!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator</strong><br />Quickly, she ate some of the other piece of mushroom and …</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Where have my&nbsp;<strong>shoulders</strong>&nbsp;gone? And my hands – where are you, hands?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice grew and grew until her&nbsp;<strong>neck</strong>&nbsp;was as long as a snake. Up and up she grew, through the branches and leaves, until her head was higher than the trees. Alice found she could move her neck just like a snake, bending this way and that. She was about to use her long neck to push her head down into the trees&nbsp;and look for her shoulders and hands, when suddenly a furious bird flew at her.</p> 
 <p><strong>Bird<br /></strong>Snake! Snake!&nbsp;<strong>You want</strong>&nbsp;my eggs!&nbsp;<strong>I know</strong>!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I'm not a snake! I'm a… I'm a little girl!</p> 
 <p><strong>Bird<br /></strong>Little girl or snake, it doesn't matter to me, you want my eggs just the same!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I don't want your eggs, really I don't!</p> 
 <p><strong>Bird<br /></strong>Then be off with you! Go away!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>The bird settled angrily into its nest. Alice ate a little of one side of the mushroom, then a little of the other, then a little of the first again until she was a good size. She decided to find her way back the door to the beautiful garden that she saw when she first arrived in Wonderland. As she walked through the forest she found a little clearing, with a small house in it, not much more than a metre or so high.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I wonder who lives here? The house is so small – anyone who lives here will surely be afraid of me!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice ate a little more of the mushroom and quickly brought herself down to the right size for this little house. Next time, Alice meets a walking fish, talks to a smiling cat and has to look after a baby. Goodbye.</p> 
 "
"<p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Hello. Alice fell down a Rabbit Hole one day and found herself in a Wonderland, where Animals talk, curious things happen and everything she eats and drinks makes her grow bigger or smaller. Now she is sitting alone. Suddenly, she heard footsteps. The White Rabbit was running towards her. He seemed to be very worried.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Oh dear! Where can I have dropped them? I must find them, or I'm sure The Duchess will&nbsp;<strong>chop</strong>&nbsp;<strong>off</strong>&nbsp;my head!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice guessed he was looking for the gloves and fan that he had dropped - but she didn't know where they were either. After all her growing and shrinking, Alice was exactly the same size as the rabbit. When the White Rabbit saw Alice, he spoke to her quite angrily.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Mary Ann! What are you doing out here? Run home this minute and get me a pair of gloves and a fan! Quickly!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>How surprised he'll be when he finds out I'm not Mary Ann!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice began to run, as the White Rabbit had told her, although she didn't quite know where she should run to. But soon, a little house appeared with the words 'W. Rabbit' written on the door.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>I won't knock on the door. The real Mary Ann might hear me.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice crept into the house and went quietly upstairs to a little bedroom… and there she found two fans, three pairs of gloves and…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Another bottle! I hope it makes me grow bigger again. I'm tired of being such a tiny little thing!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>…and sure enough, Alice began to grow. Taller and taller she grew, until…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>Ouch! My head! That's quite tall enough. That's tall enough! O-o-o-oh…</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice tried her hardest to stop growing - but it seemed to her like the harder she tried, the taller she grew. Soon Alice was so big that she filled the whole room. Her head pressed against the ceiling, her arm went out of the window and one of her feet went up the&nbsp;<strong>chimney</strong>.</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>What will become of me now?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Outside the house, a crowd started to gather. Alice heard voices.</p> 
 <p><strong>Voices<br /></strong>Oh my goodness, oh my -&nbsp;whatever could it be? What is it?</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Soon, the White Rabbit arrived.</p> 
 <p><strong>White</strong>&nbsp;<strong>Rabbit<br /></strong>What's that in the window?</p> 
 <p><strong>Voice<br /></strong>It's an arm, sir!</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>An arm? Well, it's got no business being there! Bill! Bill! Fetch the&nbsp;<strong>ladder</strong>&nbsp;and take it away!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Bill was the&nbsp;<strong>gardener</strong>. He brought a ladder and climbed up on to the roof.</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>I won't have an arm in my bedroom! Down you go Bill, down the chimney!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Poor Bill went up the ladder and tried to go down the chimney. But Alice's foot was waiting for him… with a big kick.</p> 
 <p><strong>Bill<br /></strong>Ohhhhhhhh!!!!</p> 
 <p><strong>Voices<br /></strong>Oohs and ahhs, gasps etc Is he hurt? Help him up, give him some air…</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>There! That's got rid of him! Now what will they try?</p> 
 <p><strong>Voices<br /></strong>Try the cakes!</p> 
 <p><strong>White Rabbit<br /></strong>Yes! The cakes: bring the cakes! We'll need a lot of them. That's right. Now, everybody, throw them through the other window!</p> 
 <p><strong>Alice<br /></strong>What's this…? Oh! Lots and lots of little cakes. &nbsp;I wonder…&nbsp;<strong>If I ate them, would I shrink again</strong>? They must do something… and I must get out of this house. I'll try just one of them to start with.</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>Alice ate one of the little cakes, and soon found herself to be a little smaller. She ate another and another, until at last she was just the right size to run out of the bedroom… and out of the house.</p> 
 <p><strong>Voices<br /></strong>There she is! What is it? Get her! Catch her, quickly!</p> 
 <p><strong>Narrator<br /></strong>But Alice was too fast for them. She ran far away from the White Rabbit's house, deeper and deeper into the forest until she became quite lost. She was wondering what she could eat or drink to make her grow to the right size again, when suddenly she saw in front of her a large mushroom - about the same size as herself, with a large blue&nbsp;<strong>caterpillar</strong>&nbsp;sitting on top of it, smoking a pipe and taking no notice of Alice at all. Will the caterpillar help Alice to grow again? I'll tell you next time.</p>
